Fitch Rates Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2025-1
3117 words
1 May 2025
Fitch Rating / Non Rating Action Commentary
FITRA
English
Copyright 2025 by Fitch Ratings Inc., Fitch Ratings Ltd. and its subsidiaries.

Fitch Ratings-New York-01 May 2025: Fitch Ratings has assigned ratings and Rating Outlooks to the notes issued by Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2025-1 (DEFT 2025-1). The transaction is a securitization of equipment-backed receivables originated by Dell Financial Services LLC (DFS) or its affiliates.

Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2025-1

----A-1 ; Short Term Rating; New Rating; F1+sf

----A-2 ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; AAAsf; Rating Outlook Stable

----A-3 ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; AAAsf; Rating Outlook Stable

----B ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; AAsf; Rating Outlook Stable

----C ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; Asf; Rating Outlook Stable

----D ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; BBBsf; Rating Outlook Stable

KEY RATING DRIVERS

Collateral/Obligor Performance — Strong Credit Quality: Consistent with prior DEFT transactions, DEFT 2025-1 has a high concentration of investment-grade (IG) rated obligors. The weighted-average (WA) rating of the top 10 rated obligors is 'A-'/'BBB+', stronger than the WA rating of 'BBB'/'BBB-' in DEFT 2024-2. The number of non-IG obligors in DEFT 2025-1 remains a sizable portion of the pool, but these obligors have historically demonstrated low default and loss experience.

Concentration Risk — Obligor Concentration: The largest obligor, the top 10 obligors, and the top 20 obligors represent 4.97%, 32.12%, and 44.71% of DEFT 2025-1, up modestly from 4.91%, 30.16%, and 42.52% of DEFT 2024-2, respectively. While there is high concentration within the top 10 obligors, concentration declines significantly thereafter and is more consistent with traditional small-ticket equipment ABS transactions. Furthermore, seven of the top 10 obligors are IG entities, in line with recent DEFT transactions.

Given the unique collateral characteristics of DEFT transactions, a modified obligor concentration approach is the primary rating driver as opposed to the stressed loss approach.

Forward-Looking Approach to Derive Rating-Case Loss Proxy — Normalizing Asset Performance: DFS-owned portfolio loss performance in the small and medium-sized business (SMB) segment remains strong, at or below the portfolio's historical average, improving from the weakness in late 2020 and early 2021. Default rates have been low in the public and large institution (PLI) segment due to the sturdy credit profiles of these obligors.

All DFS-sponsored securitizations exhibited low cumulative net losses (CNLs), while the performance of DEFT transactions between 2022 and 2023 has continued to normalize, compared with the strong performance observed during the pandemic.

The rating case CNL proxy for DEFT 2025-1 is 1.30%, down from 1.45% in DEFT 2024-2. However, the ratings are determined based on a modified obligor coverage approach due to the transaction's high concentration of IG obligors among the top 20 obligors and its shorter contract terms than those of other equipment ABS.

Structural Analysis — Sufficient Credit Enhancement (CE): All classes benefit from a non-declining cash reserve account funded at 1.00% of the initial discounted pool balance and initial overcollateralization (OC) equal to 4.30% of the discounted pool balance. Total initial hard CE for the class A, B, C, and D notes is 12.40%, 10.80%, 8.60%, and 5.30%, respectively.

While CE levels for classes A and D are lower than in DEFT 2024-2, classes B and C have had increases. Specifically, the CE for class B increased to 10.80% from 10.58%, and for class C, it rose to 8.60% from 8.18%. Conversely, CE for class A decreased to 12.40% from 12.58%, and for class D, it dropped to 5.30% from 5.58%.

Additionally, all classes benefit from 3.05% per annum of excess spread. The structure can support the default of the top 10, eight, six, and four non-IG obligors.

Operational and Servicing Risk — Quality of Origination, Underwriting and Servicing: DFS has demonstrated adequate abilities as originator, underwriter, and servicer, as evidenced by historical delinquency and loss performance of securitized trusts and its owned and managed portfolio.

Fitch's base case CNL expectation, which does not include a margin of safety and is not used in Fitch's quantitative analysis to assign ratings, is 0.70%. This is based on Fitch's economic outlook and managed pool and historical securitization performance.

RATING SENSITIVITIES

Factors that Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Negative Rating Action/Downgrade

Unanticipated increases in the frequency of defaults could produce CNL levels higher than the rating case CNL proxy and would likely result in declines of CE and the remaining net loss coverage levels available to the notes. In addition, unanticipated declines in recoveries could also result in a decline in net loss coverage. Decreased net loss coverage may make certain note ratings susceptible to potential negative rating actions, depending on the extent of the decline in coverage.

Fitch conducted a sensitivity of the obligor concentration coverage approach in which the ratings of the top 20 obligors were assumed to have been downgraded by a single rating category. For example, an obligor currently rated 'BBB' would be downgraded to 'BB'. No rating migration applies to unrated entities, as they were already categorized as non-IG in Fitch's primary analysis. The results of this analysis showed that all the classes would experience a multi-notch downgrade. The severity of these downgrades is driven by the 'BBB' range obligors being downgraded to non-IG.

The top 20 obligors downgraded to non-IG increases to 12 from eight. This results in higher loss hurdles when compared to the primary scenario and the ratings of the DEFT 2025-1 notes would be downgraded. Fitch considers this analysis conservative as it does not take into consideration the CE build as the transaction de-levers. Downgrades of entities occur over a longer period, which would give the transaction time to de-lever as the collateral pool amortizes. Furthermore, Fitch considers the likelihood of a simultaneous downgrade of these entities unlikely and, therefore, views this scenario as remote.

Fitch conducts sensitivity analyses by stressing both a transaction's initial rating case CNL proxy and recovery rate assumptions and examining the rating implications on all classes of issued notes. The CNL sensitivity stresses the rating case CNL proxy to the level necessary to reduce each rating by one full category, to non-IG (BBsf) and to 'CCCsf' based on the break-even loss coverage provided by the CE structure. In addition, Fitch applies 1.5x and 2.0x increases to the rating case CNL proxy, which represent moderate and severe stresses, respectively.

Fitch also evaluates the impact of stressed recovery rates on an equipment ABS structure and rating impact with a 50% haircut. However, Fitch's rating analysis for DEFT 2025-1 only assumes a 3.50% recovery credit. Given the low recovery assumption, Fitch did not conduct a recovery rate sensitivity for this rating analysis.

Factors that Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Positive Rating Action/Upgrade

Stable to improved asset performance, driven by stable delinquencies and defaults would lead to increasing CE levels and consideration for potential upgrades.

Fitch conducted a sensitivity of the aforementioned obligor concentration coverage approach in which the ratings of the top 20 obligors were assumed to have been upgraded by a single rating category. For example, an obligor currently rated 'BBB-' was assumed to have been upgraded to 'A-' at close. No rating migration applies to unrated entities, as they were already categorized as non-IG in Fitch's primary analysis. This results in lower loss hurdles than in the primary scenario and the commensurate ratings would remain unchanged.

USE OF THIRD PARTY DUE DILIGENCE PURSUANT TO SEC RULE 17G -10

Fitch was provided with Form ABS Due Diligence-15E (Form 15E) as prepared by PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP. The third-party due diligence described in Form 15E focused on the comparison and recomputation of certain information with respect to 175 contracts from the preliminary collateral pool of assets in connection with DEFT 2025-1. Fitch considered this information in its analysis, and it did not have an effect on our analysis or conclusions.

REFERENCES FOR SUBSTANTIALLY MATERIAL SOURCE CITED AS KEY DRIVER OF RATING

The principal sources of information used in the analysis are described in the Applicable Criteria.

REPRESENTATIONS, WARRANTIES AND ENFORCEMENT MECHANISMS

A description of the transaction's representations, warranties and enforcement mechanisms (RW&Es) that are disclosed in the offering document and which relate to the underlying asset pool is available by clicking the link to the Appendix. The appendix also contains a comparison of these RW&Es to those Fitch considers typical for the asset class as detailed in the Special Report titled 'Representations, Warranties and Enforcement Mechanisms in Global Structured Finance Transactions'.

ESG Considerations

The highest level of ESG credit relevance is a score of '3', unless otherwise disclosed in this section. A score of '3' means ESG issues are credit-neutral or have only a minimal credit impact on the entity, either due to their nature or the way in which they are being managed by the entity. Fitch's ESG Relevance Scores are not inputs in the rating process; they are an observation on the relevance and materiality of ESG factors in the rating decision. For more information on Fitch's ESG Relevance Scores, visit https://www.fitchratings.com/topics/esg/products#esg-relevance-scores[https://www.fitchratings.com/topics/esg/products#esg-relevance-scores].

Fitch Expects to Rate Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2025-1; Issues Presale

Fitch Ratings-New York-21 April 2025: Fitch Ratings expects to assign ratings and Rating Outlooks to the notes issued by Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2025-1 (DEFT 2025-1). The transaction is a securitization of equipment-backed receivables originated by Dell Financial Services LLC (DFS) or its affiliates.

Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2025-1

----A-1 ; Short Term Rating; Expected Rating; F1+(EXP)sf

----A-2 ; Long Term Rating; Expected Rating; AAA(EXP)sf; Rating Outlook Stable

----A-3 ; Long Term Rating; Expected Rating; AAA(EXP)sf; Rating Outlook Stable

----B ; Long Term Rating; Expected Rating; AA(EXP)sf; Rating Outlook Stable

----C ; Long Term Rating; Expected Rating; A(EXP)sf; Rating Outlook Stable

----D ; Long Term Rating; Expected Rating; BBB(EXP)sf; Rating Outlook Stable

Fitch Rates Dell's Senior Unsecured Debt Offering 'BBB'
2716 words
26 March 2025
Fitch Rating / Non Rating Action Commentary
FITRA
English
Copyright 2025 by Fitch Ratings Inc., Fitch Ratings Ltd. and its subsidiaries.

Fitch Ratings-Toronto-26 March 2025: Fitch Ratings has assigned a 'BBB' rating to Dell International L.L.C.'s (Dell) and EMC Corporation's new 3-, 5,-, 7- and 10-year unsecured issuances. The company will use the offering's net proceeds for general corporate purposes, which may include the repayment of debt.

Key Rating Drivers

PC Market Leader: Fitch anticipates the mature personal computer (PC) market will continue to experience cyclical growth fluctuations aligned with GDP over the long term. Dell's Client Solutions Group (CSG) comprises about half of Dell's sales. CSG is positioned to benefit from tailwinds in AI-related performance demands, PC refresh cycles, and the growth of hybrid working environments, which could boost demand for monitors and peripherals.

Positioned for AI Growth: Dell is a market leader in servers and multiple storage categories, showing adaptability despite competition from cloud solutions. The Infrastructure Solutions Group (ISG) segment is well-positioned to benefit from demand for both traditional and more expensive AI servers. Generative AI and the potential for increased data growth are tailwinds for the ISG segment, which could enhance Fitch's assessment of the industry's growth potential if they materialize over time. Dell's full product portfolio and services support its competitive positioning, including within the growing AI hardware market.

Declining Core Leverage: Fitch uses core EBITDA leverage in its assessment of Dell, excluding the estimated contribution of Dell Financial Services (DFS). Fitch forecasts Dell to maintain leverage below the upgrade sensitivity of 2.0x over the rating horizon

Capacity for Shareholder Returns from High FCF: Fitch's forecast average pre-dividend annual FCF of around $4 billion to $5 billion annually through the rating horizon provides capacity for continued post-shareholder return debt reductions. Dell's financial policy allocates more than 80% of FCF to shareholder returns through dividends and share repurchases. The remaining FCF goes toward M&A and leverage activities. Since the majority of shareholder returns typically are from discretionary share buybacks, Dell has the flexibility to adjust distribution levels during years of weaker FCF.

Strategic Focus on Smaller M&A: Dell's M&A strategy focuses on tuck-in acquisitions that enhance its intellectual property or strengthen its position in strategic markets like AI. An improving trend in Dell's financial structure provides some ratings headroom for potential M&A involving debt financing. Consistent with Dell's tuck-in acquisition strategy and the expectation that any smaller strategic acquisitions would have a lag before meaningfully affecting top-line growth, Fitch does not attribute material M&A contributions to revenue during its forecast period.

Parent and Subsidiary IDRs Equalized: Fitch equalizes the Issuer-Default Ratings (IDRs) of Dell Technologies Inc (BBB/F2/Positive), the public holding company and its wholly owned indirect subsidiaries that are issuers of debt (Dell Inc., Dell International LLC and EMC Corporation). Under Fitch's Parent and Subsidiary Linkage Criteria, this follows the stronger subsidiary and weaker parent relationship, with the consolidated credit profile reflecting both open access and control, as well as the absence of legal ring fencing.

Peer Analysis

Hewlett Packard Enterprise Company (HPE; BBB+/Stable) has more software content and models, which are relatively higher margin compared to Dell's product portfolio, and has historically had a more conservative financial structure. Dell aims to distribute over 80% FCF, compared to HPE's 60%, which is expected to decrease if HPE closes its Juniper Networks Inc. acquisition.

Compared with HP Inc. (HP; BBB+/Stable), Dell's business profile benefits from its exposure to the server and storage market. HP has a comparable PC business and faces secular challenges in its printing business. HP's financial profile is stronger than Dell's, with higher FCF margins and a historically more conservative financial structure. HP's shareholder return policy is more aggressive than HPE and Dell, with a plan to return approximately 100% of FCF to shareholders while under 2.0x gross leverage.

Key Assumptions

--Annual forecast revenue modestly up sequentially, supported by the expectation improvement in enterprise demand and refresh cycle. Revenue during the latter half of forecast is expected to see mid-single-digit growth in ISG as AI-related demand continues, as well as mid- to low-single-digit growth in CSG;

-- Modest EBITDA margin increases during the forecast period, supported by a focus on cost controls and expense control actions;

--Steady capex of 2.5%-3.0% of revenue, consistent with historic annual levels;

--Minimum 80% of FCF used for shareholder returns. Per share dividends grow 10% annually, in line with Dell's financial policy;

--Capitalization (debt/equity) attributable to DFS and related to core leverage calculation steady at 4.0x through the forecast period. An adjustment is made to sustain an allowable leverage level at a standalone DFS, based on input from Fitch's Non-Bank Financial Institutions group;

--Base interest rates applicable to the company's RCF obligations reflects current secured overnight financing rate forward curve. No facility draws are forecast.

RATING SENSITIVITIES

Factors that Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Negative Rating Action/Downgrade

--Decline in organic revenue from sustained market share losses in CSG and ISG segments;

--Core EBITDA leverage sustained above 2.5x and adjusted FCF to core debt, with volatility, averaging below 20%.

Factors that Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Positive Rating Action/Upgrade

--Consistent organic revenue growth from higher EBITDA market-share gains in ISG segments;

--Core EBITDA leverage sustained below 2.0x and low volatility of adjusted FCF to core debt, sustained near

20%.

Liquidity and Debt Structure

At the end of fiscal 2025, Dell's liquidity consisted of approximately $3.6 billion of readily available cash and an undrawn $6.0 billion RCF maturing November 2027. Dell's revolving facilities also support a $5 billion unused CP program. Forecast post-dividend FCF further support Dell's liquidity and reduce refinancing risk.

Dell's next notable senior unsecured maturity period is in its fiscal 2027 when $4.25 billion of notes mature. Excluding the current issue, maturities of approximately $10 billion of Dell's outstanding unsecured notes are staggered between 2029 and 2051.

Issuer Profile

Dell is a leading global diversified technology infrastructure provider with a comprehensive portfolio of IT hardware, software and service solutions spanning traditional and emerging, multicloud technologies.

Summary of Financial Adjustments

Fitch deconsolidates, including a profitability estimate and debt proxy related to DFS, financing activities to calculate core EBITDA and core debt for core leverage for Dell Technologies, Inc. A maximum allowable debt to equity ratio for the financing business of 4:1 is applied and an adjustment to Dell's debt level to maintain this is made.

Date of Relevant Committee

07 October 2024

to access Fitch's latest quarterly Global Corporates Macro and Sector Forecasts data file which aggregates key data points used in our credit analysis. ESG Considerations

Dell has an ESG Relevance Score of '4' for Governance Structure as Michael Dell is a controlling shareholder of the company's common stock and there exists key man risk. This has a negative impact on the credit profile and is relevant to the rating in conjunction with other factors.

Fitch Rates Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2024-2
3116 words
16 October 2024
Fitch Rating / Non Rating Action Commentary
FITRA
English
Copyright 2024 by Fitch Ratings Inc., Fitch Ratings Ltd. and its subsidiaries.

Fitch Ratings-New York-16 October 2024: Fitch Ratings has assigned ratings and Rating Outlooks to the notes issued by Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2024-2 (DEFT 2024-2). The transaction is a securitization of equipment-backed receivables originated by Dell Financial Services LLC (DFS) or its affiliates.

DEFT 2024-2

----A-1 ; Short Term Rating; New Rating; F1+sf

----A-2 ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; AAAsf; Rating Outlook Stable

----A-3 ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; AAAsf; Rating Outlook Stable

----B ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; AAsf; Rating Outlook Stable

----C ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; Asf; Rating Outlook Stable

----D ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; BBBsf; Rating Outlook Stable

KEY RATING DRIVERS

Collateral/Obligor Performance — Strong Credit Quality: Consistent with prior DEFT transactions, DEFT 2024-2 has a high concentration of investment-grade (IG) rated obligors. The weighted-average (WA) rating of the top 10 rated obligors is 'BBB'/'BBB-', the lowest amount among recent transactions, driven by an increase in 'BBB' rated top obligors. Although the amount of non-IG obligors in DEFT 2024-2 is lower than in recent transactions, they remain a sizable portion of the pool. These obligors have historically demonstrated low default and loss experience.

Concentration Risk — Obligor Concentration: The largest obligor, the top 10 obligors and the top 20 obligors represent 4.91%, 30.16% and 42.52% of DEFT 2024-2, respectively. These levels are lower than DEFT 2024-1, and more in line with DEFT 2023-3. While there is high concentration within the top 10 obligors, concentration declines significantly after that and is more consistent with traditional, small-ticket equipment ABS transactions. Furthermore, eight of the top 10 obligors are IG entities, compared to five IG obligors among the top 10 in DEFT 2024-1.

Given the unique collateral characteristics of DEFT transactions, a modified obligor concentration approach is the primary rating driver as opposed to the stressed loss approach.

Forward-Looking Approach to Derive Rating Case Loss Proxy — Resilient but Normalizing Asset Performance: DFS-owned portfolio loss performance in the small and medium business (SMB) segment remains strong, at or below the portfolio's historical average, improving from the weakness in late 2020 and early 2021. The public and large institutions (PLI) segment has seen low default rates due to the sturdy credit profiles of these obligors. All DFS-sponsored securitizations showed low cumulative net losses (CNLs), but performance of recent DEFT transactions has been normalizing more quickly compared with the strength shown during the pandemic.

The rating case CNL proxy for DEFT 2024-2 is 1.45%, but the ratings are determined based on a modified obligor coverage approach given the transaction's high concentration of IG obligors among the top 20 obligors and shorter contract terms than those of other equipment ABS.

Structural Analysis — Sufficient Credit Enhancement (CE): All classes benefit from a non-declining cash reserve account funded at 1.08% of the initial discounted pool balance and initial overcollateralization (OC) equal to 4.50% of the discounted pool balance. Total initial hard CE for the class A, B, C and D notes is 12.58%, 10.58%, 8.18% and 5.58%, respectively. The initial hard CE levels for DEFT 2024-2 are lower than DEFT 2024-1 but in line with other recent DEFT transactions.

In addition, all classes benefit from 2.59% per annum of excess spread. The structure can support the default of the top 10, eight, six and four non-IG obligors.

Operational and Servicing Risk — Quality of Origination, Underwriting and Servicing: DFS has demonstrated adequate abilities as originator, underwriter and servicer, as evidenced by historical delinquency and loss performance of securitized trusts and its owned and managed portfolio.

Fitch's base case CNL expectation, which does not include a margin of safety and is not used in Fitch's quantitative analysis to assign ratings, is 0.80%. This is based on Fitch's economic outlook and forecast projections.

RATING SENSITIVITIES

Factors that Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Negative Rating Action/Downgrade

Unanticipated increases in the frequency of defaults could produce CNL levels higher than the rating case CNL proxy, and would likely result in declines of CE and remaining net loss coverage levels available to the notes. In addition, unanticipated declines in recoveries could also result in a decline in net loss coverage. Decreased net loss coverage may make certain note ratings susceptible to potential negative rating actions, depending on the extent of the decline in coverage.

Fitch conducts a sensitivity of the obligor concentration coverage approach in which the ratings of the top 20 obligors were assumed to have been downgraded by a single rating category. For example, an obligor currently rated 'BBB' would be downgraded to 'BB'. No rating migration applies to unrated entities, as they were already categorized as non-IG in Fitch's primary analysis. The results of this analysis showed that all of the classes would experience a multi-notch downgrade. The severity of these downgrades is driven by the 'BBB' range obligors being downgraded to non-IG.

The top 20 obligors downgraded to non-IG increases to 15 from seven. This results in higher loss hurdles when compared to the primary scenario, and the ratings of the DEFT 2024-2 notes would be downgraded. Fitch considers this analysis conservative as it does not take into consideration the CE build as the transaction de-levers. In reality, downgrades of entities occur over a longer period, which would give the transaction time to de-lever as the collateral pool amortizes. Furthermore, Fitch considers the likelihood of a simultaneous downgrade of these entities unlikely and, therefore, views this scenario as remote.

Fitch conducts sensitivity analyses by stressing both a transaction's initial rating case CNL proxy and recovery rate assumptions and examining the rating implications on all classes of issued notes. The CNL sensitivity stresses the rating case CNL proxy to the level necessary to reduce each rating by one full category, to non-IG (BBsf) and to 'CCCsf' based on the break-even loss coverage provided by the CE structure. In addition, Fitch applies 1.5x and 2.0x increases to the rating case CNL proxy, which represent moderate and severe stresses, respectively.

Fitch also evaluates the impact of stressed recovery rates on an equipment ABS structure and rating impact with a 50% haircut. However, Fitch's rating analysis for DEFT 2024-2 only assumes a 3.50% recovery credit. Given the low recovery assumption, Fitch did not conduct a recovery rate sensitivity for this rating analysis.

Factors that Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Positive Rating Action/Upgrade

Stable to improved asset performance driven by stable delinquencies and defaults would lead to increasing CE levels and consideration for potential upgrades.

Fitch conducted a sensitivity of the aforementioned obligor concentration coverage approach in which the ratings of the top 20 obligors were assumed to have been upgraded by a single rating category. For example, an obligor currently rated 'BBB-' was assumed to have been upgraded to 'A-' at close. No rating migration applies to unrated entities, as they were already categorized as non-IG in Fitch's primary analysis. This results in lower loss hurdles when compared to the primary scenario and the commensurate ratings would remain unchanged.

USE OF THIRD PARTY DUE DILIGENCE PURSUANT TO SEC RULE 17G -10

Fitch was provided with Form ABS Due Diligence-15E (Form 15E) as prepared by PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP . The third-party due diligence described in Form 15E focused on the comparison and recomputation of certain information with respect to 175 contracts from the preliminary collateral pool of assets in connection with DEFT 2024-2. Fitch considered this information in its analysis and it did not have an effect on Fitch's analysis or conclusions.

Fitch Affirms Dell Technologies at 'BBB'/'F2'; Outlook Revised to Positive
3475 words
7 October 2024
Fitch Rating / Non Rating Action Commentary
FITRA
English
Copyright 2024 by Fitch Ratings Inc., Fitch Ratings Ltd. and its subsidiaries.

Fitch Ratings-Toronto-07 October 2024: Fitch Ratings has affirmed the Long-Term Issuer Default Ratings (IDRs) and Short-Term IDRs of Dell Technologies Inc. (Dell), Dell International LLC and EMC Corporation at 'BBB' and 'F2'. Dell International LLC and EMC Corporation's senior unsecured ratings and short-term CP ratings are affirmed at 'BBB' and 'F2'. Dell Inc's IDR is affirmed at 'BBB' and its senior unsecured ratings at 'BBB-'. The Rating Outlook has been revised to Positive from Stable.

Dell's rating is informed by its leading market positions, demand pipeline in its server and storage lines, and its liquidity position. It also considers Dell's competitive industry profile and the potential impact on performance from macroeconomic headwinds. The Positive Outlook reflects Dell's core EBITDA leverage that is below 2.0x, its position to benefit from increased AI hardware spending, and potential EBITDA margin improvements in its ISG segment.

Key Rating Drivers

Declining Core Leverage: Fitch utilizes core EBITDA leverage, Fitch's calculation that excludes the estimated contribution of Dell Financial Services (DFS), as part of its assessment of Dell. Core leverage for Dell's latest fiscal year ended Feb. 2, 2024 was 1.7x, modestly below the upgrade sensitivity of 2.0x. We expect this to be about 1.6x at fiscal YE 2025. Dell's Positive Outlook is supported by Fitch's expectation that core leverage will continue to decrease with EBITDA improvements and be maintained around 1.5x during the forecast period.

PC Market Leader: Fitch anticipates that the mature PC market will continue to experience cyclical growth fluctuations aligned with GDP over the long term. Dell's Client Solutions Group (CSG) makes up about half of Dell's sales, and a percentage of sales mix is down through 1H25 due to the relative performance of its Infrastructure Solutions Group (ISG). CSG is positioned to benefit from tailwinds in artificial intelligence (AI) related performance demands, a refresh cycles of PCs and the growth of hybrid working environments, which could boost demand for monitors and peripherals.

Positioned for AI Growth: Dell is a market leader in servers and multiple storage categories, showing adaptability despite competition from cloud solutions. The ISG is well-positioned to benefit from demand for both traditional and more expensive AI servers, as results through Dell's 1H25 have demonstrated. Generative AI and potential for increased data growth present a tailwind for the ISG segment, which could enhance Fitch's assessment of the industry's growth potential if they materialize over time. Dell's full product portfolio and services support its competitive positioning, including within the growing AI hardware market.

Capacity for High FCF Returns to Shareholders: Forecast average pre-dividend annual FCF of around $4 billion to $5 billion annually through the rating horizon provides capacity for continued post-shareholder return debt reductions. Dell's financial policy prioritizes more than 80% of FCF to shareholder returns through dividends and share repurchases. The remaining FCF goes toward M&A and leverage activities. Since the majority of shareholder returns typically come from discretionary share buybacks, Dell has the flexibility to adjust distribution levels during years of weaker FCF.

While Dell increased its dividend 20% at the beginning of fiscal 2025, Fitch's expects the less flexible dividends to be broadly around only 30% of pre-dividend FCF during its forecast. Under Fitch's base case, Dell is expected to exceed its 80% minimum return target while maintaining its credit profile.

Strategic Smaller M&A: Dell's M&A strategy focuses on tuck-in acquisitions that add to its intellectual property or increases its position in strategic markets, such as AI. An improving trend in Dell's financial structure provides some ratings headroom for potential M&A that uses a debt finance component. Consistent with Dell's tuck-in acquisition signaling and the expectation that any smaller strategic acquisitions would have a lag period before meaningfully affecting top-line growth, Fitch does not attribute material M&A contributions to revenue during its forecast period.

Parent and Subsidiary IDRs Equalized: Fitch equalizes the IDRs of Dell, the public holding company, and its wholly owned indirect subsidiaries that are issuers of debt (Dell Inc., Dell International LLC and EMC Corporation). Under Fitch's "Parent and Subsidiary Linkage Criteria," this follows the stronger subsidiary/weaker parent relationship with the consolidated credit profile reflecting both open access and control, as well as the absence of legal ring fencing.

Dell Inc.'s senior unsecured notes, which represent approximately $1 billion of debt, are rated one notch below its IDR due to the structural subordination of these notes, which are not guaranteed by Dell, Dell International or EMC Corporation.

Derivation Summary

Hewlett Packard Enterprise Company's (HPE; BBB+/Stable) financial structure has traditionally been more conservative than Dell's. Fitch forecasts HPE's core EBITDA level which has been a relative credit profile difference with Dell, net of its planned Juniper acquisition, to be 1.1x at fiscal 2024 (ending Oct. 31, 2024), However, HPE's EBITDA should increase meaningfully above Dell's level to about 3x pro forma HPE's Juniper transaction. The difference is expected to normalize over the next two years as HPE reduces net leverage toward its target of 2x.

There are modest differences in financial policies between the companies, with Dell targeting an 80% distribution of FCF compared to HPE's 60%. HPE believes M&A is a core component of its expected growth, while Dell targets smaller, strategic value tuck-in acquisitions. HPE's profitability benefits from a higher EBITDA margin than Dell, partly due to HPE's higher margin software exposure. In contrast, about half of Dell's sales mix comes from relatively lower-margin PC and peripherals sales.

Compared with HP Inc. (HP; BBB+/Stable), Dell's industry profile sector-specific key factor rating assigned in our ratings navigator is two notches higher at 'bbb-'. Dell's business profile benefits from its exposure to the server and storage market. HP has a comparable PC business and faces secular challenges in its printing business. HP's financial profile is stronger than Dell's, with higher FCF margins and a historically more conservative financial structure. HP has the most aggressive shareholder return policy, compared with HPE and Dell, with a plan to return approximately 100% of FCF to shareholders while under 2.0x gross leverage.

Key Assumptions

Fitch's key assumptions within our rating case for the issuer include:

--ISG revenue improves in fiscal 2025 yoy about 27% and CSG in fiscal 2025 yoy is about flat informed by 1H25 results, guidance and the expectation for continued server demand momentum;

--Fiscal 2026 forecast revenue modestly up sequentially, directionally consistent with Fitch's "Global Economic Outlook - September 2024," supported by the expectation improvement in enterprise demand and eventual refresh cycle. Revenue during the latter half of forecast is expected to see midsingle-digit growth in ISG as AI-related demand continues, as well as mid- to low single-digit growth in CSG;

--An EBITDA margin of approximately 10% is expected for fiscal 2025, informed by actual fiscal 1H25 results. Modest margin increases during the forecast period supported by a focus on cost controls and expense control actions;

--Steady capex of 2.5%-3.0% of revenue, consistent with historic annual levels;

--Minimum 80% of FCF utilized for shareholder returns. Per share dividends grow 10% annually, in line with Dell's financial policy;

--Capitalization (debt/equity) attributable to DFS and related to core leverage calculation steady at 4.0x through forecast period. A capital injection from cash on hand is made to DFS to sustain an allowable leverage level from Fitch's Non-Bank Financial Institutions group;

--Base interest rates applicable to the company's revolving credit facility obligations reflects current secured overnight financing rate forward curve declining to 2.8% from 5.0% during the forecast period. No facility draws are forecast.

RATING SENSITIVITIES

Fitch could stabilize the Outlook for the 'BBB' ratings if we expect core leverage to be sustained above 2.0x.

Factors that Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Positive Rating Action/Upgrade

--Consistent organic revenue growth from higher EBITDA market-share gains in ISG segments;

--Core EBITDA leverage sustained below 2.0x and low volatility of adjusted FCF to core debt, sustained near 20%.

Factors that Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Negative Rating Action/Downgrade

--Decline in organic revenue from sustained market share losses in CSG and ISG segments;

--Core EBITDA leverage sustained above 2.5x adjusted and adjusted FCF to core debt with volatility averaging below 20%.

Liquidity and Debt Structure

Cash in Excess of Operational Needs: At 2Q fiscal 2025 Dell's liquidity position consisted of approximately $4.56 billion of readily available cash and an undrawn $6.0 billion revolving credit facility maturing November 2027. Excluding Dell's revolving facilities, which also support a $5 billion unused commercial paper program, this level of cash provides a healthy buffer to support cyclical needs in excess of a $4 billion to $5 billion level of cash that Dell management estimates it requires on hand to operate its business.

Forecast post-dividend FCF between fiscal 2026 and fiscal 2028 of approximately $3 billion to $3.5 billion annually further support Dell's liquidity and reduce refinancing risk. Dell's next notable maturity period is in its fiscal 2027 when $4.25 billion of senior unsecured notes, which Dell cut by $1 billion during fiscal 2024, matures. Approximately $10 billion of Dell's outstanding unsecured notes mature at staggered dates between 2029 and 2051.

Issuer Profile

Dell is a leading global diversified technology infrastructure provider with a comprehensive portfolio of IT hardware, software and service solutions spanning traditional and emerging, multicloud technologies.

Summary of Financial Adjustments

Fitch deconsolidates a profitability estimate and debt proxy related to Dell Financial Services (DFS) financing activities to calculate core EBITDA and core debt for core leverage for Dell Technologies, Inc. A maximum allowable debt to equity ratio for the financing business of 4:1 is applied.

REFERENCES FOR SUBSTANTIALLY MATERIAL SOURCE CITED AS KEY DRIVER OF RATING

The principal sources of information used in the analysis are described in the Applicable Criteria.

MACROECONOMIC ASSUMPTIONS AND SECTOR FORECASTS

to access Fitch's latest quarterly Global Corporates Macro and Sector Forecasts data file which aggregates key data points used in our credit analysis. Fitch's macroeconomic forecasts, commodity price assumptions, default rate forecasts, sector key performance indicators and sector-level forecasts are among the data items included.

ESG Considerations

Dell has an ESG Relevance Score of '4' for Governance Structure as Michael Dell is a controlling shareholder of the company's common stock and there exists key man risk. This has a negative impact on the credit profile and is relevant to the rating in conjunction with other factors.

The highest level of ESG credit relevance is a score of '3', unless otherwise disclosed in this section. A score of '3' means ESG issues are credit-neutral or have only a minimal credit impact on the entity, either due to their nature or the way in which they are being managed by the entity. Fitch's ESG Relevance Scores are not inputs in the rating process; they are an observation on the relevance and materiality of ESG factors in the rating decision. For more information on Fitch's ESG Relevance Scores, visit https://www.fitchratings.com/topics/esg/products#esg-relevance-scores[https://www.fitchratings.com/topics/esg/products#esg-relevance-scores].

Fitch Expects to Rate Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2024-2; Issues Presale
3058 words
3 October 2024
Fitch Rating / Non Rating Action Commentary
FITRA
English
Copyright 2024 by Fitch Ratings Inc., Fitch Ratings Ltd. and its subsidiaries.

Related Content:

Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2024-2 (US ABS): https://pro.fitchratings.com/research/article/RPT_10286873[https://pro.fitchratings.com/research/article/RPT_10286873]

Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2024-2 - Appendix: https://pro.fitchratings.com/research/article/RPT_10286875[https://pro.fitchratings.com/research/article/RPT_10286875]

Fitch Ratings-New York-03 October 2024: Fitch Ratings expects to assign ratings and Rating Outlooks to the notes issued by Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2024-2 (DEFT 2024-2). The transaction is a securitization of equipment-backed receivables originated by Dell Financial Services LLC (DFS) or its affiliates.

Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2024-2

----A-1 ; Short Term Rating; Expected Rating; F1+(EXP)sf

----A-2 ; Long Term Rating; Expected Rating; AAA(EXP)sf; Rating Outlook Stable

----A-3 ; Long Term Rating; Expected Rating; AAA(EXP)sf; Rating Outlook Stable

----B ; Long Term Rating; Expected Rating; AA(EXP)sf; Rating Outlook Stable

----C ; Long Term Rating; Expected Rating; A(EXP)sf; Rating Outlook Stable

----D ; Long Term Rating; Expected Rating; BBB(EXP)sf; Rating Outlook Stable

KEY RATING DRIVERS

Collateral/Obligor Performance — Strong Credit Quality: Consistent with prior DEFT transactions, DEFT 2024-2 has a high concentration of investment-grade (IG) rated obligors. The weighted-average (WA) rating of the top 10 rated obligors is 'BBB'/'BBB-', the lowest amount among recent transactions, driven by an increase in 'BBB' rated top obligors. Although the amount of non-IG obligors in DEFT 2024-2 is lower than in recent transactions, they remain a sizable portion of the pool. These obligors have historically demonstrated low default and loss experience.

Concentration Risk — Obligor Concentration: The largest obligor, the top 10 obligors and the top 20 obligors represent 4.91%, 30.16% and 42.52% of DEFT 2024-2, respectively. These levels are lower than DEFT 2024-1, and more in line with DEFT 2023-3. While there is high concentration within the top 10 obligors, concentration declines significantly after that and is more consistent with traditional, small-ticket equipment ABS transactions. Furthermore, eight of the top 10 obligors are IG entities, compared to five IG obligors among the top 10 in DEFT 2024-1.

Given the unique collateral characteristics of DEFT transactions, a modified obligor concentration approach is the primary rating driver as opposed to the stressed loss approach.

Forward-Looking Approach to Derive Rating Case Loss Proxy — Resilient but Normalizing Asset Performance: DFS-owned portfolio loss performance in the small and medium business (SMB) segment remains strong, at or below the portfolio's historical average, improving from the weakness in late 2020 and early 2021. The public and large institutions (PLI) segment has seen low default rates due to the sturdy credit profiles of these obligors. All DFS-sponsored securitizations showed low cumulative net losses (CNLs), but performance of recent DEFT transactions has been normalizing more quickly compared with the strength shown during the pandemic.

The rating case CNL proxy for DEFT 2024-2 is 1.45%, but the ratings are determined based on a modified obligor coverage approach given the transaction's high concentration of IG obligors among the top 20 obligors and shorter contract terms than those of other equipment ABS.

Structural Analysis — Sufficient Credit Enhancement (CE): All classes benefit from a non-declining cash reserve account funded at 1.00% of the initial discounted pool balance and initial overcollateralization (OC) equal to 4.50% of the discounted pool balance. Total initial hard CE for the class A, B, C and D notes is 12.50%, 10.50%, 8.10% and 5.50%, respectively. The initial hard CE levels for DEFT 2024-2 are lower than DEFT 2024-1 but in line with other recent DEFT transactions.

In addition, all classes benefit from 2.65% per annum of excess spread. The structure can support the default of the top 10, eight, six and four non-IG obligors.

Operational and Servicing Risk — Quality of Origination, Underwriting and Servicing: DFS has demonstrated adequate abilities as originator, underwriter and servicer, as evidenced by historical delinquency and loss performance of securitized trusts and its owned and managed portfolio.

Fitch's base case CNL expectation, which does not include a margin of safety and is not used in Fitch's quantitative analysis to assign ratings, is 0.80%. This is based on Fitch's economic outlook and forecast projections.

RATING SENSITIVITIES

Factors that Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Negative Rating Action/Downgrade

Unanticipated increases in the frequency of defaults could produce CNL levels higher than the rating case CNL proxy, and would likely result in declines of CE and remaining net loss coverage levels available to the notes. In addition, unanticipated declines in recoveries could also result in a decline in net loss coverage. Decreased net loss coverage may make certain note ratings susceptible to potential negative rating actions, depending on the extent of the decline in coverage.

Fitch conducts a sensitivity of the obligor concentration coverage approach in which the ratings of the top 20 obligors were assumed to have been downgraded by a single rating category. For example, an obligor currently rated 'BBB' would be downgraded to 'BB'. No rating migration applies to unrated entities, as they were already categorized as non-IG in Fitch's primary analysis. The results of this analysis showed that all of the classes would experience a multi-notch downgrade. The severity of these downgrades is driven by the 'BBB' range obligors being downgraded to non-IG.

The top 20 obligors downgraded to non-IG increases to 15 from seven. This results in higher loss hurdles when compared to the primary scenario and the ratings of the DEFT 2024-2 notes would be downgraded. Fitch considers this analysis conservative as it does not take into consideration the CE build as the transaction de-levers. In reality, downgrades of entities occur over a longer period, which would give the transaction time to de-lever as the collateral pool amortizes. Furthermore, Fitch considers the likelihood of a simultaneous downgrade of these entities unlikely and, therefore, views this scenario as remote.

Fitch conducts sensitivity analyses by stressing both a transaction's initial rating case CNL proxy and recovery rate assumptions and examining the rating implications on all classes of issued notes. The CNL sensitivity stresses the rating case CNL proxy to the level necessary to reduce each rating by one full category, to non-IG (BBsf) and to 'CCCsf' based on the break-even loss coverage provided by the CE structure. In addition, Fitch applies 1.5x and 2.0x increases to the rating case CNL proxy, which represent moderate and severe stresses, respectively.

Fitch also evaluates the impact of stressed recovery rates on an equipment ABS structure and rating impact with a 50% haircut. However, Fitch's rating analysis for DEFT 2024-2 only assumes a 3.50% recovery credit. Given the low recovery assumption, Fitch did not conduct a recovery rate sensitivity for this rating analysis.

Factors that Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Positive Rating Action/Upgrade

Stable to improved asset performance driven by stable delinquencies and defaults would lead to increasing CE levels and consideration for potential upgrades.

Fitch conducted a sensitivity of the aforementioned obligor concentration coverage approach in which the ratings of the top 20 obligors were assumed to have been upgraded by a single rating category. For example, an obligor currently rated 'BBB-' was assumed to have been upgraded to 'A-' at close. No rating migration applies to unrated entities, as they were already categorized as non-IG in Fitch's primary analysis. This results in lower loss hurdles when compared to the primary scenario and the commensurate ratings would remain unchanged.

USE OF THIRD PARTY DUE DILIGENCE PURSUANT TO SEC RULE 17G -10

Fitch was provided with Form ABS Due Diligence-15E (Form 15E) as prepared by PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP. The third-party due diligence described in Form 15E focused on the comparison and recomputation of certain information with respect to 175 contracts from the preliminary collateral pool of assets in connection with DEFT 2024-2. Fitch considered this information in its analysis and it did not have an effect on our analysis or conclusions.

The principal sources of information used in the analysis are described in the Applicable Criteria.

The appendix also contains a comparison of these RW&Es to those Fitch considers typical for the asset class as detailed in the Special Report titled 'Representations, Warranties and Enforcement Mechanisms in Global Structured Finance Transactions'.

A score of '3' means ESG issues are credit-neutral or have only a minimal credit impact on the entity, either due to their nature or the way in which they are being managed by the entity. Fitch's ESG Relevance Scores are not inputs in the rating process; they are an observation on the relevance and materiality of ESG factors in the rating decision. Fitch Rates Dell's Senior Unsecured Debt Offering 'BBB'
2903 words
1 October 2024
Fitch Rating / Non Rating Action Commentary
FITRA
English
Copyright 2024 by Fitch Ratings Inc., Fitch Ratings Ltd. and its subsidiaries.

Fitch Ratings-Toronto-01 October 2024: Fitch Ratings has assigned a 'BBB' rating to Dell International L.L.C.'s and EMC Corporation's (as co-issuers) new unsecured issuances maturing 2030 and 2035. The company will use the offering's proceeds to redeem the $1 billion outstanding 5.85% notes maturing July, 2025. They will issue a redemption notice at the same times as the offering. Any excess amounts will go toward general corporate purposes.

Key Rating Drivers

PC and Server Market Leader: Fitch anticipates that the mature PC market will continue to experience cyclical growth fluctuations aligned with GDP over the long term. Dell's Client Solutions Group (CSG) makes up about half of Dell's sales and a percentage of sales mix is down through 1H25 due to the relative performance of its Infrastructure Solutions Group (ISG). CSG is positioned to benefit from tailwinds in artificial intelligence (AI) related performance demands, a refresh cycles of PCs, and the growth of hybrid working environments, which could boost demand for monitors and peripherals.

Dell is a market leader in servers with top positions in multiple storage categories. Its ISG and related data center spending has shown adaptability and resilience, even as alternative technologies, such as competitor cloud solutions offer alternatives. The ISG is well-positioned to benefit from current demand for both traditional and AI servers. Generative AI and potential for increased data growth present a tailwind for the ISG segment, which could enhance Fitch's assessment of the industry's growth potential if these benefits materialize over time.

Core Leverage: Fitch utilizes core EBITDA leverage, Fitch's calculation of which excludes the estimated contribution of Dell Financial Services (DFS), as part of its assessment of Dell. Core leverage for Dell's latest fiscal year ended February 2, 2024 was 1.7x, modestly below the upgrade sensitivity of 2.0x. Fitch expects core leverage to further decrease toward 1.5x during the forecast period as EBITDA improves.

Capacity for High FCF Returns to Shareholders: Forecast average pre-dividend annual FCF of around $4 billion to $5 billion annually through the rating horizon provides capacity for continued post-shareholder return debt reductions. Dell's financial policy prioritizes more than 80% of FCF to shareholder returns through dividends and share repurchases. The remaining FCF goes towards M&A and leverage activities. Since the majority of shareholder returns typically come from discretionary share buy backs, Dell has the flexibility to adjust distribution levels during years of weaker FCF. Under Fitch's base case, Dell is expected to exceed the 80% minimum return target while maintaining its credit profile.

Strategic Smaller M&A: Dell's M&A strategy focuses on tuck-in acquisitions that add to its intellectual property or increases its position in strategic markets, such as AI. An improving trend in Dell's financial structure provides some ratings headroom for potential M&A that uses a debt finance component. Consistent with Dell's tuck-in acquisition signaling and the expectation that any smaller strategic acquisitions would have a lag period before meaningfully affecting top-line growth, Fitch does not attribute material M&A contributions to revenue during its forecast period.

Parent Subsidiary IDRs Equalized: Fitch equalizes the IDR's of Dell Technologies, Inc., the public holding company, and its wholly owned indirect subsidiaries that issue debt: Dell Inc., Dell International LLC and EMC Corporation. Under Fitch's "Parent and Subsidiary Linkage Criteria" this follows the stronger subsidiary weaker parent relationship with the consolidated credit profile reflecting both open access and control, as well as the absence of legal ring fencing.

Derivation Summary

Hewlett Packard Enterprise Company's (HPE; BBB+/Stable) financial structure has traditionally been more conservative than Dell's. Fitch forecasts HPE's core EBITDA level--which has been a relative credit profile difference with Dell--net of its planned Juniper acquisition, to be 1.1x at fiscal 2024 (ending Oct. 31, 2024), However, HPE's EBITDA should increase meaningfully above Dell's level, to about 3x proforma HPE's Juniper transaction. The difference is expected to normalize over the next two years as HPE reduces net leverage towards its target of 2x.

There are modest differences in financial policies between the companies, with Dell targeting an 80% distribution of FCF, compared to HPE's 60%. HPE believes M&A is a core component of its expected growth, while Dell targets smaller, strategic value tuck-in acquisitions. HPE's profitability benefits from a higher EBITDA margin than Dell, partly due to HPE's higher margin software exposure. In contrast, about half of Dell's sales mix comes from relatively lower-margin PC and peripherals sales.

Compared with HP Inc. (HP; BBB+/Stable), Dell's industry profile sector-specific key factor rating assigned in our ratings navigator is two notches higher at 'bbb-'. Dell's business profile benefits from its exposure to the server and storage market. HP has a comparable PC business and faces secular challenges in its printing business. HP's financial profile is stronger than Dell's, with higher FCF margins and a historically more conservative financial structure. HP has the most aggressive shareholder return policy, compared with HPE and Dell, with a plan to return approximately 100% of FCF to shareholders while under 2.0x gross leverage.

Key Assumptions

--CSG revenues improve in fiscal 2025 yoy about 27% and ISG in fiscal 2025 yoy is about flat informed by 1H25 results, guidance and the expectation for continued server demand momentum;

--Fiscal 2026 forecast revenues modestly up sequentially, directionally consistent with Fitch's Global Economic Outlook - September 2024, supported by the expectation improvement in enterprise demand and eventual refresh cycle. Revenues during the latter half of forecast are expected to see mid-single-digit growth in ISG as AI related demand continues, as well as mid to low-single-digit growth in CSG;

--Steady capex of 2.5%-3.0% of revenue, consistent with historic annual levels;

--Minimum 80% of FCF utilized for shareholder returns. Per share dividends grow 10% annually, in line with Dell's financial policy;

--Capitalization (debt/equity) attributable to DFS and related to core leverage calculation steady at 4.0x through forecast period. A capital injection from cash on hand is made to DFS to sustain an allowable leverage level from Fitch's Non-Bank Financial Institutions group;

--Base interest rates applicable to the company's revolving credit facility obligations reflects current secured overnight financing rate forward curve declining from 5.00% to 2.8% during the forecast period. No facility draws are forecast.

RATING SENSITIVITIES

Factors That Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Positive Rating Action/Upgrade

--Consistent organic revenue growth from profitable market-share gains in CSG and ISG segments;

--Core EBITDA leverage sustained below 2.0x and adjusted FCF to core debt sustained near 30%.

Factors That Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Negative Rating Action/Downgrade

--Decline in organic revenue from sustained market-share losses in CSG and ISG segments;

--Core EBITDA leverage sustained above 2.5x adjusted and adjusted FCF to core debt sustained near 20%.

Liquidity and Debt Structure

Cash in Excess of Operational Needs: At 2Q fiscal 2025 Dell's liquidity position consisted of approximately $4.56 billion of readily available cash and an undrawn $6.0 billion revolving credit facility maturing November 2027. Excluding Dell's revolving facilities, which also support a $5 billion unused commercial paper program, this level of cash provides a healthy buffer to support cyclical needs in excess of a $4 billion to $5 billion level of cash that Dell management estimates it requires on hand to operate its business.

Issuer Profile

Dell is a leading global diversified technology infrastructure provider, with a comprehensive portfolio of IT hardware, software and service solutions spanning both traditional and emerging, multi-cloud technologies.

Summary of Financial Adjustments

Fitch deconsolidates a profitability estimate and debt proxy related to Dell Financial Services (DFS) financing activities to calculate Core EBITDA and Core debt for Core Leverage for Dell Technologies, Inc. A maximum allowable debt to equity ratio for the financing business of 4:1 is applied.

24 October 2023

Fitch Rates Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2024-1
3054 words
17 April 2024
Fitch Rating / Non Rating Action Commentary
FITRA
English
Copyright 2024 by Fitch Ratings Inc., Fitch Ratings Ltd. and its subsidiaries.

Fitch Ratings-Toronto-17 April 2024: Fitch Ratings has assigned ratings and Rating Outlooks to the notes issued by Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2024-1 (DEFT 2024-1). The transaction is a securitization of equipment receivables originated by Dell Financial Services L.L.C. (DFS) or its affiliates.

Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2024-1

----A-1 ; Short Term Rating; New Rating; F1+sf

----A-2 ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; AAAsf; Rating Outlook Stable

----A-3 ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; AAAsf; Rating Outlook Stable

----B ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; AAsf; Rating Outlook Stable

----C ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; Asf; Rating Outlook Stable

----D ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; BBBsf; Rating Outlook Stable

KEY RATING DRIVERS

Collateral/Obligor Performance — Strong Credit Quality: Consistent with prior DEFT transactions, DEFT 2024-1 has a high concentration of investment-grade (IG) obligors. The weighted-average (WA) rating of the top 10 rated obligors is about 'BBB+'/'A-', consistent with DEFT 2023-3. Although the amount of non-IG obligors in DEFT 2024-1 is lower than in recent transactions, there remains a sizable portion in the pool; however, these obligors have historically demonstrated low default and loss experience.

Concentration Risk — Obligor Concentration: The largest obligor, the top 10 obligors and the top 20 obligors represent 4.72%, 31.75% and 45.71% of DEFT 2024-1, respectively. These levels are higher than DEFT 2023-3 but more in line with DEFT 2023-2. While there is high concentration within the top 10 obligors, concentration declines significantly after that and is more consistent with traditional small-ticket equipment ABS transactions. Furthermore, the top 10 obligors are mostly IG entities.

Given the unique collateral characteristics of DEFT transactions, a modified obligor concentration approach is the primary rating driver as opposed to the stressed loss approach.

Forward-Looking Approach to Derive Rating Case Loss Proxy — Strong but Normalizing Asset Performance: DFS-owned portfolio loss performance in the small and medium business (SMB) segment remains strong, at or below the portfolio's historical average, improving from the weakness observed in late 2020 and early 2021. The public and large institutions (PLI) segment has seen low default rates due to the sturdy credit profiles of these obligors. All DFS-sponsored securitizations showed low cumulative net losses (CNLs), but performance of recent DEFT transactions has shown a normalizing trend compared with the strength shown through the pandemic.

The rating case CNL proxy for DEFT 2024-1 is 1.20%, but the ratings are determined based on a modified obligor coverage approach given the transaction's high concentration of IG obligors among the top 20 obligors and shorter contract terms than those of other equipment ABS.

Structural Analysis — Sufficient Credit Enhancement: Total initial hard CE for the class A, B, C and D notes is 13.65%, 12.60%, 10.35% and 7.40%, respectively. The initial hard CE levels for DEFT 2024-1 are higher than DEFT 2023-3 but similar to DEFT 2023-2. The DEFT 2024-1 class A, B, and C notes benefit from subordination of 6.25%, 5.20% and 2.95%, respectively.

Additionally, all classes benefit from a non-declining cash reserve account funded at 1.00% of the initial discounted pool balance and initial overcollateralization (OC) equal to 6.40% of the discounted pool balance. All classes also benefit from 2.48% per annum of excess spread. The structure can support the default of the top 10, eight, six and four non-IG obligors.

Operational and Servicing Risk — Quality of Origination, Underwriting and Servicing: DFS has demonstrated adequate abilities as originator, underwriter and servicer, as evidenced by historical delinquency and loss performance of securitized trusts and its owned and managed portfolio.

Fitch's base case CNL expectation, which does not include a margin of safety and is not used in Fitch's quantitative analysis to assign ratings, is 0.70%. This is based on Fitch's economic outlook and forecasted projections.

RATING SENSITIVITIES

Factors that Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Negative Rating Action/Downgrade

Unanticipated increases in the frequency of defaults could produce CNL levels higher than the rating case CNL proxy and would likely result in declines of CE and remaining net loss coverage levels available to the notes. Additionally, unanticipated declines in recoveries could also result in a decline in net loss coverage. Decreased net loss coverage may make certain note ratings susceptible to potential negative rating actions, depending on the extent of the decline in coverage.

Fitch conducts a sensitivity of the obligor concentration coverage approach in which the ratings of the top 20 obligors were assumed to have been downgraded by a single rating category. For example, an obligor currently rated 'BBB' would be downgraded to 'BB'. No rating migration applies to unrated entities, as they were already categorized as non-IG in Fitch's primary analysis. The results of this analysis showed that all of the classes would experience a multi-notch downgrade. The severity of these downgrades is driven by the 'BBB' range obligors being downgraded to non-IG.

The top 20 obligors downgraded to non-IG increases to nine from one. This results in higher loss hurdles when compared with the primary scenario and the ratings to the DEFT 2024-1 notes would be downgraded. Fitch considers this analysis conservative, as it does not take into consideration the CE build as the transaction de-levers. In reality, downgrades of entities occur over a longer period, which would give the transaction time to de-lever as the collateral pool amortizes. Furthermore, Fitch considers the likelihood of a simultaneous downgrade of these entities unlikely and, therefore, views this scenario as remote.

Fitch conducts sensitivity analyses by stressing both a transaction's initial rating case CNL proxy and recovery rate assumptions and examining the rating implications on all classes of issued notes. The CNL sensitivity stresses the rating case CNL proxy to the level necessary to reduce each rating by one full category, to non-IG (BBsf) and to 'CCCsf' based on the break-even loss coverage provided by the CE structure. Additionally, Fitch applies 1.5x and 2.0x increases to the rating case CNL proxy, which represent moderate and severe stresses, respectively.

Fitch also evaluates the impact of stressed recovery rates on an equipment ABS structure and rating impact with a 50% haircut. However, Fitch's rating analysis for DEFT 2024-1 only assumes a 3.50% recovery credit. Given the low recovery assumption, Fitch did not conduct a recovery rate sensitivity for this rating analysis.

Factors that Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Positive Rating Action/Upgrade

Stable to improved asset performance driven by stable delinquencies and defaults would lead to increasing CE levels and consideration for potential upgrades.

Fitch conducted a sensitivity of the aforementioned obligor concentration coverage approach in which the ratings of the top 20 obligors were assumed to have been upgraded by a single rating category. For example, an obligor currently rated 'BBB-' was assumed to have been upgraded to 'A-' at close. No rating migration applies to unrated entities, as they were already categorized as non-IG in Fitch's primary analysis. This results in lower loss hurdles when compared to the primary scenario and the commensurate ratings would remain unchanged.

USE OF THIRD PARTY DUE DILIGENCE PURSUANT TO SEC RULE 17G -10

Fitch was provided with Form ABS Due Diligence-15E (Form 15E) as prepared by PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP. The third-party due diligence described in Form 15E focused on the comparison and recomputation of certain information with respect to 175 contracts from the preliminary collateral pool of assets in connection with DEFT 2024-1. Fitch considered this information in its analysis and it did not have an effect on Fitch's analysis or conclusions.

Fitch Expects to Rate Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2024-1; Issues Presale
3085 words
3 April 2024
Fitch Rating / Non Rating Action Commentary
FITRA
English
Copyright 2024 by Fitch Ratings Inc., Fitch Ratings Ltd. and its subsidiaries.

Related Content:

Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2024-1 (US ABS): https://app.fitchconnect.com/search/research/article/RPT_10266456[https://app.fitchconnect.com/search/research/article/RPT_10266456]

Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2024-1 - Appendix: https://app.fitchconnect.com/search/research/article/RPT_10266607[https://app.fitchconnect.com/search/research/article/RPT_10266607]

Fitch Ratings-Toronto-03 April 2024: Fitch Ratings expects to assign ratings and Rating Outlooks to the notes issued by Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2024-1 (DEFT 2024-1). The transaction is a securitization of equipment backed receivables originated by Dell Financial Services L.L.C. (DFS) or its affiliates.

Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2024-1

----A-1 ; Short Term Rating; Expected Rating; F1+(EXP)sf

----A-2 ; Long Term Rating; Expected Rating; AAA(EXP)sf; Rating Outlook Stable

----A-3 ; Long Term Rating; Expected Rating; AAA(EXP)sf; Rating Outlook Stable

----B ; Long Term Rating; Expected Rating; AA(EXP)sf; Rating Outlook Stable

----C ; Long Term Rating; Expected Rating; A(EXP)sf; Rating Outlook Stable

----D ; Long Term Rating; Expected Rating; BBB(EXP)sf; Rating Outlook Stable

KEY RATING DRIVERS

Collateral/Obligor Performance — Strong Credit Quality: Consistent with prior DEFT transactions, DEFT 2024-1 has a high concentration of investment-grade (IG) obligors. The weighted-average (WA) rating of the top 10 rated obligors is about 'BBB+'/'A-', consistent with DEFT 2023-3. Although the amount of non-IG obligors in DEFT 2024-1 is lower than in recent transactions, there remains a sizable portion in the pool; however, these obligors have historically demonstrated low default and loss experience.

Concentration Risk — Obligor Concentration: The largest obligor, the top 10 obligors and the top 20 obligors represent 4.72%, 31.75% and 45.71% of DEFT 2024-1, respectively. These levels are higher than DEFT 2023-3 but more in line with DEFT 2023-2. While there is high concentration within the top 10 obligors, concentration declines significantly after that and is more consistent with traditional small-ticket equipment ABS transactions. Furthermore, the top 10 obligors are mostly IG entities.

Given the unique collateral characteristics of DEFT transactions, a modified obligor concentration approach is the primary rating driver as opposed to the stressed loss approach.

Forward-Looking Approach to Derive Rating Case Loss Proxy — Strong but Normalizing Asset Performance: DFS-owned portfolio loss performance in the small and medium business (SMB) segment remains strong, at or below the portfolio's historical average, improving from the weakness observed in late 2020 and early 2021. The public and large institutions (PLI) segment has seen low default rates due to the sturdy credit profiles of these obligors. All DFS-sponsored securitizations showed low cumulative net losses (CNLs), but performance of recent DEFT transactions has shown a normalizing trend compared with the strength shown through the pandemic.

The rating case CNL proxy for DEFT 2024-1 is 1.20%, but the ratings are determined based on a modified obligor coverage approach given the transaction's high concentration of IG obligors among the top 20 obligors and shorter contract terms than those of other equipment ABS.

Structural Analysis — Sufficient Credit Enhancement: Total initial hard CE for the class A, B, C and D notes is 13.65%, 12.60%, 10.35% and 7.40%, respectively. The initial hard CE levels for DEFT 2024-1 are higher than DEFT 2023-3 but similar to DEFT 2023-2. The DEFT 2024-1 class A, B, and C notes benefit from subordination of 6.25%, 5.20% and 2.95%, respectively.

Additionally, all classes benefit from a non-declining cash reserve account funded at 1.00% of the initial discounted pool balance and initial overcollateralization (OC) equal to 6.40% of the discounted pool balance. All classes also benefit from 2.27% per annum of excess spread. The structure can support the default of the top 10, eight, six and four non-IG obligors.

Operational and Servicing Risk — Quality of Origination, Underwriting and Servicing: DFS has demonstrated adequate abilities as originator, underwriter and servicer, as evidenced by historical delinquency and loss performance of securitized trusts and its owned and managed portfolio.

Fitch's base case CNL expectation, which does not include a margin of safety and is not used in Fitch's quantitative analysis to assign ratings, is 0.70%. This is based on Fitch's economic outlook and forecasted projections.

RATING SENSITIVITIES

Factors that Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Negative Rating Action/Downgrade

Unanticipated increases in the frequency of defaults could produce CNL levels higher than the rating case CNL proxy and would likely result in declines of CE and remaining net loss coverage levels available to the notes. Additionally, unanticipated declines in recoveries could also result in a decline in net loss coverage. Decreased net loss coverage may make certain note ratings susceptible to potential negative rating actions, depending on the extent of the decline in coverage.

Fitch conducts a sensitivity of the obligor concentration coverage approach in which the ratings of the top 20 obligors were assumed to have been downgraded by a single rating category. For example, an obligor currently rated 'BBB' would be downgraded to 'BB'. No rating migration applies to unrated entities, as they were already categorized as non-IG in Fitch's primary analysis. The results of this analysis showed that all of the classes would experience a multi-notch downgrade. The severity of these downgrades is driven by the 'BBB' range obligors being downgraded to non-IG.

The top 20 obligors downgraded to non-IG increases to nine from one. This results in higher loss hurdles when compared with the primary scenario and the ratings to the DEFT 2024-1 notes would be downgraded. Fitch considers this analysis conservative, as it does not take into consideration the CE build as the transaction de-levers. In reality, downgrades of entities occur over a longer period, which would give the transaction time to de-lever as the collateral pool amortizes. Furthermore, Fitch considers the likelihood of a simultaneous downgrade of these entities unlikely and, therefore, views this scenario as remote.

Fitch conducts sensitivity analyses by stressing both a transaction's initial rating case CNL proxy and recovery rate assumptions and examining the rating implications on all classes of issued notes. The CNL sensitivity stresses the rating case CNL proxy to the level necessary to reduce each rating by one full category, to non-IG (BBsf) and to 'CCCsf' based on the break-even loss coverage provided by the CE structure. Additionally, Fitch applies 1.5x and 2.0x increases to the rating case CNL proxy, which represent moderate and severe stresses, respectively.

Fitch also evaluates the impact of stressed recovery rates on an equipment ABS structure and rating impact with a 50% haircut. However, Fitch's rating analysis for DEFT 2024-1 only assumes a 3.50% recovery credit. Given the low recovery assumption, Fitch did not conduct a recovery rate sensitivity for this rating analysis.

Factors that Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Positive Rating Action/Upgrade

Stable to improved asset performance driven by stable delinquencies and defaults would lead to increasing CE levels and consideration for potential upgrades.

Fitch conducted a sensitivity of the aforementioned obligor concentration coverage approach in which the ratings of the top 20 obligors were assumed to have been upgraded by a single rating category. For example, an obligor currently rated 'BBB-' was assumed to have been upgraded to 'A-' at close. No rating migration applies to unrated entities, as they were already categorized as non-IG in Fitch's primary analysis. This results in lower loss hurdles when compared to the primary scenario and the commensurate ratings would remain unchanged.

USE OF THIRD PARTY DUE DILIGENCE PURSUANT TO SEC RULE 17G -10

Fitch was provided with Form ABS Due Diligence-15E (Form 15E) as prepared by PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP. The third-party due diligence described in Form 15E focused on the comparison and recomputation of certain information with respect to 175 contracts from the preliminary collateral pool of assets in connection with DEFT 2024-1. Fitch considered this information in its analysis and it did not have an effect on Fitch's analysis or conclusions.

The principal sources of information used in the analysis are described in the Applicable Criteria.

REPRESENTATIONS, WARRANTIES AND ENFORCEMENT MECHANISMS

The appendix also contains a comparison of these RW&Es to those Fitch considers typical for the asset class as detailed in the Special Report titled 'Representations, Warranties and Enforcement Mechanisms in Global Structured Finance Transactions'.

ESG Considerations

The highest level of ESG credit relevance is a score of '3', unless otherwise disclosed in this section. A score of '3' means ESG issues are credit-neutral or have only a minimal credit impact on the entity, either due to their nature or the way in which they are being managed by the entity. Fitch's ESG Relevance Scores are not inputs in the rating process; they are an observation on the relevance and materiality of ESG factors in the rating decision. Fitch Ratings: Dell?s Ratings Unaffected by Debt Tender
1537 words
4 December 2023
Fitch Rating / Non Rating Action Commentary
FITRA
English
Copyright 2023 by Fitch Ratings Inc., Fitch Ratings Ltd. and its subsidiaries.

Fitch Ratings-Chicago/Toronto-04 December 2023: Dell Technologies Inc?s credit profile benefits from the announced cash tender, but its Long-Term Issuer Default Ratings (IDRs) and Short-Term IDRs of 'BBB' and 'F2', respectively, are unaffected by it.

On Dec. 4 Dell announced a cash tender for up to $500 million in aggregate debt prioritized over seven senior unsecured debt issuances. Fitch views the gross debt reduction favorably. The bottom line impact is likely to be modestly tempered by the relatively lower coupon rate of the higher acceptance priority targeted issues, which benefits leverage but has a smaller impact on interest coverage. After taking account of an assumed successful $500 million gross debt reduction, Fitch forecasts core EBITDA leverage to be approximately 1.8x at fiscal YE 2024. Although this transaction supports reducing leverage toward Dell's 1.5x core leverage long-term target, it is not enough to affect the rating.

This tender follows $2.2 billion of senior unsecured debt reductions made during the first six months of fiscal 2024 completed through a combination of an approximately $1 billion debt tender, $1 billion of maturing debt repaid with cash and opportunistic open market operations.

Dell's rating reflects its leading market positions, improving core EBITDA leverage below 2.0x that has benefitted from gross debt reduction actions, and Dell's liquidity position. It also considers Dell's competitive industry profile, current consumer and enterprise spending restraint, as well as potential macroeconomic headwinds.
