Fitch Affirms Dell Technologies at 'BBB'/'F2'; Outlook Stable
3186 words
25 October 2023
Fitch Rating / Non Rating Action Commentary
FITRA
English
Copyright 2023 by Fitch Ratings Inc., Fitch Ratings Ltd. and its subsidiaries.

Fitch Ratings-Toronto-25 October 2023: Fitch Ratings has affirmed the Long-Term Issuer Default Ratings (IDR) and Short-Term IDRs of Dell Technologies Inc. (Dell), Dell International LLC and EMC Corporation at 'BBB', and 'F2'. Dell International LLC and EMC Corporation's senior unsecured ratings and short-term CP ratings are affirmed at 'BBB' and 'F2'. Dell Inc's IDR is affirmed at 'BBB' and its senior unsecured ratings at 'BBB-'. The Rating Outlook is Stable.

Dell's rating reflects its leading market positions, improving core EBITDA leverage below 2.0x that has benefitted from gross debt reduction actions, and Dell's liquidity position. It also considers Dell's competitive industry profile, current consumer and enterprise spending restraint, as well as potential macroeconomic headwinds.

Key Rating Drivers

PC and Server Market Leader: The PC market is largely mature and Fitch anticipates related revenues, which have returned down to pre-pandemic levels, to continue to be affected by consumer and enterprise spending restraint, as well as pandemic demand pull through in the short term. Over the longer-term, Fitch anticipates market growth to continue to be cyclically affected and to broadly fluctuate with economic demand aligned with GDP.

Dell's Client Solutions Group (CSG), which comprises around 57% of the company's sales mix, is positioned to benefit from tailwinds in artificial intelligence should that accelerate refresh cycles of PC's, as well as longer term hybrid working environments that Dell's market position in monitors and its peripherals growth emphasis could benefit from. Profitability within CSG has benefited from an increase in sales mix to more profitable commercial sales, which contributed over 80% of segment sales in the first half of fiscal 2024.

Dell is the market leader in servers and has leading positions in multiple storage categories. Its Infrastructure Solutions Group (ISG) and related data center spending has proven adaptable and resilient as alternative technologies such as competitor cloud solutions provide substitution options. Generative artificial intelligence (AI) and the related potential increase for data growth requirements provides a tailwind for the ISG segment that could improve Fitch's assessment of the industry's growth potential if these benefits are demonstrated over time.

Core Leverage: Fitch utilizes core EBITDA leverage, which excludes the estimated contribution of Dell Financial Services (DFS), as part of its assessment of Dell. Core leverage is forecast to be 1.9x at fiscal YE 2024, modestly below the upgrade sensitivity of 2.0x and Fitch expects it to further decrease during the forecast period as EBITDA improves, trending towards Dell's 1.5x core leverage long-term target.

Discretionary Debt Reductions: During the first six months of fiscal 2024, leverage benefitted from approximately $2.2 billion in senior unsecured debt reductions completed through a combination of an approximately $1 billion debt tender, $1 billion of maturing debt repaid with cash and opportunistic open market operations. The open market bond repurchases targeted lower coupon 2041 and 2051 senior unsecured bond issues, which benefits leverage, but has a smaller impact on interest coverage.

Forecast average pre-dividend annual FCF in excess of $5 billion thorough the rating horizon provides capacity for continued post shareholder return debt reductions. Dell's financial policy prioritizes 80%+ of FCF to shareholder returns through dividends and share repurchases, with M&A and leverage activities allocated the remaining FCF.

Strategic Smaller M&A: Dell's M&A strategy is focused on tuck-in acquisitions that add to its intellectual property or increase their position in strategic markets such as AI. An improving trend in Dell's financial structure provides some ratings headroom for potential M&A that uses a debt finance component. Consistent with Dell's tuck in acquisition signaling, as well as the expectation that any smaller strategic acquisitions would have a lag period before meaningfully impacting top line growth, Fitch does not attribute material M&A contributions to revenue during its forecast period.

Parent Subsidiary IDR's Equalized: Fitch equalizes the IDR's of Dell, the public holding company, and its wholly owned indirect subsidiaries that are issuers of debt, Dell Inc., Dell International LLC and EMC Corporation. Under Fitch's Parent and Subsidiary Linkage Criteria this follows the stronger subsidiary weaker parent relationship with the consolidated credit profile reflecting both open access and control, as well as the absence of legal ring fencing.

Dell Inc's senior unsecured notes, which represent approximately $1 billion of debt, are rated one notch below its IDR due to the structural subordination of these notes, which are not guaranteed by Dell, Dell International or EMC Corporation.

Derivation Summary

Dell's financial structure has improved to be closer to that of Hewlett Packard Enterprise Company (HPE; BBB+/Stable). Core EBITDA of both companies is between 1.5x-2.0x. There is a modest different in financial policies, with Dell targeting to distribute 80%+ of FCF compared to 60% of FCF at HPE. This is partially explainable by HPE considering M&A to be a core component of its expected growth, compared to Dell who is targeting smaller more strategic value tuck in acquisitions. HPE's profitability benefits from higher EBITDA margin than Dell partially attributable to HPE's software exposure and nearly two-thirds mix Dell's sales mix from relatively lower margin PC and peripherals sales.

Compared to HP Inc. (HP; BBB+/Stable) Dell's industry profile rating sub-factor is one notch above HP, as Dell business profile relatively benefits from its exposure to the server and storage market. HP has a comparable PC business to Dell and faces secular challenges in its printing business. HP's financial profile is stronger than Dell's, with higher FCF margins and a historically more conservative financial structure. HP Inc has the most aggressive shareholder return policy compared to HPE and Dell, with a plan to return approximately 100% of FCF to shareholders while under 2.0x gross leverage.

Key Assumptions

--ISG and CSG revenues improve in fiscal 2H24 over fiscal 1H24 continuing on fiscal 2Q24 trend, but remain tempered by broad customer spending restraint;

--Fiscal 2025 revenues modestly up sequentially, directionally informed by "Global Economic Outlook - September 2023" and the expectation of some improvement in Enterprise demand. Revenues during latter half of forecast mid-single-digit growth in ISG and mid- to low-single-digit growth in CSG;

--EBITDA margins in fiscal 2024 informed by fiscal 1H24 margins of approximately 10%. Modest margin increases during forecast period due to focus on cost controls and late fiscal 2023 and fiscal 2024 expense reduction actions;

--Steady Capex of 2.5%-3.0% of revenue, consistent with historic annual levels;

--Minimum 80% of FCF utilized for shareholder returns. Current $5 billion repurchase authorization extended during forecast. Dividends grow 10% annually;

--Capitalization (Debt/Equity) attributable to DFS and related to Core Leverage calculation steady at 4.0x through forecast period. A capital injection from cash on hand is made to DFS to sustain a Fitch Non-Bank Financial Institution group determined allowable leverage level;

--Base interest rates applicable to the company's revolving credit facility obligations reflects current SOFR forward curve declining from 5.25% to 4.00% by the end of the forecast period. No facility draws are forecast.

RATING SENSITIVITIES

Factors that could, individually or collectively, lead to positive rating action/upgrade:

--Consistent organic revenue growth from profitable market-share gains in CSG and ISG segments;

--Core EBITDA leverage sustained below 2.0x and adjusted FCF to core debt sustained near 30%.

Factors that could, individually or collectively, lead to negative rating action/downgrade:

--Decline in organic revenue from sustained market-share losses in CSG and ISG segments;

--Core EBITDA leverage sustained above 2.5x adjusted and adjusted FCF to core debt sustained near 20%.

Liquidity and Debt Structure

Cash in Excess of Operational Needs: At 2Q fiscal 2024 Dell's liquidity position consisted of approximately $8.4 billion of readily available cash and an undrawn $6.0 billion revolving credit facility maturing November 2027. Excluding Dell's revolving facilities, which also support a $5 billion unused commercial paper program, this level of cash provides a healthy buffer to support cyclical needs in excess of a $4 billion to $5 billion level of cash that Dell management estimates it requires on hand to operate its business.

Forecast FCF between fiscal 2025 and fiscal 2027 of approximately $4 billion annually further support Dell's liquidity and abate refinancing risk when $1 billion, $1 billion and $5.25 billion or senior unsecured notes mature respectively.

Issuer Profile

Dell is a leading global diversified technology infrastructure provider, with a comprehensive portfolio of IT hardware, software and service solutions spanning both traditional and emerging, multi-cloud technologies.

Summary of Financial Adjustments

Fitch deconsolidates a profitability estimate and debt proxy related to Dell Financial Services (DFS) financing activities to calculate Core EBITDA and Core debt for Core Leverage for Dell Technologies, Inc. A maximum allowable debt to equity ratio for the financing business of 4:1 is applied.

REFERENCES FOR SUBSTANTIALLY MATERIAL SOURCE CITED AS KEY DRIVER OF RATING

The principal sources of information used in the analysis are described in the Applicable Criteria.

ESG Considerations

The highest level of ESG credit relevance is a score of '3', unless otherwise disclosed in this section. A score of '3' means ESG issues are credit-neutral or have only a minimal credit impact on the entity, either due to their nature or the way in which they are being managed by the entity. Fitch's ESG Relevance Scores are not inputs in the rating process; they are an observation on the relevance and materiality of ESG factors in the rating decision. For more information on Fitch's ESG Relevance Scores, visit https://www.fitchratings.com/topics/esg/products#esg-relevance-scores[https://www.fitchratings.com/topics/esg/products#esg-relevance-scores].

Document FITRA00020231025ejap002p9


Fitch Rates Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2023-3
3042 words
18 October 2023
Fitch Rating / Non Rating Action Commentary
FITRA
English
Copyright 2023 by Fitch Ratings Inc., Fitch Ratings Ltd. and its subsidiaries.

Fitch Ratings-New York-18 October 2023: Fitch Ratings has assigned ratings and Rating Outlooks to the notes issued by Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2023-3 (DEFT 2023-3). The transaction is a securitization of equipment receivables originated by Dell Financial Services L.L.C. (DFS) or its affiliates.

Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2023-3

----A1 ; Short Term Rating; New Rating; F1+sf

----A2 ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; AAAsf; Rating Outlook Stable

----A3 ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; AAAsf; Rating Outlook Stable

----B ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; AAsf; Rating Outlook Stable

----C ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; Asf; Rating Outlook Stable

----D ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; BBBsf; Rating Outlook Stable

KEY RATING DRIVERS

Collateral/Obligor Performance ? Strong Credit Quality: Consistent with prior DEFT transactions, DEFT 2023-3 has a high concentration of investment-grade (IG) obligors. The weighted-average (WA) rating of the top 10 rated obligors is about 'A-'/'BBB+', stronger than the two recent transactions in 2023. Although the amount of non-IG obligors in DEFT 2023-3 is lower than in recent transactions, there remains a sizable portion, but these obligors have historically demonstrated low default and loss experience.

Concentration Risk ? Obligor Concentration: The largest obligor, the top-10 obligors and the top 20 obligors represent 4.69%, 28.69% and 39.93% of DEFT 2023-3, respectively. These levels are lower than DEFT 2023-2 and 2023-1 transactions. While there is high concentration within the top 10 obligors, concentration declines significantly after that and is more consistent with traditional small-ticket equipment ABS transactions. Furthermore, the top 10 obligors are mostly IG entities.

Given the unique collateral characteristics of DEFT transactions, a modified obligor concentration approach is the primary rating driver as opposed to the stressed loss approach.

Forward-Looking Approach to Derive Base-Case Loss Proxy ? Strong but Normalizing Asset Performance: Loss performance in the small and medium business (SMB) segment remains strong, at or below the portfolio's historical average, improving from the weakness in the late 2020 and early 2021. The public and large institutions (PLI) segment has seen low default rates due to the sturdy credit profiles of these obligors. All DFS-sponsored securitizations showed low cumulative net losses (CNLs), but performance of recent DEFT transactions has shown a normalizing trend compared with the strength shown through the pandemic.

The base case CNL proxy for DEFT 2023-3 is 1.20%, but the ratings are determined based on a modified obligor coverage approach given the transaction's high concentration of IG obligors among the top 20 obligors and shorter contract terms than those of other equipment ABS.

Structural Analysis ? Sufficient Credit Enhancement: All classes benefit from a cash reserve account and overcollateralization (OC). Total initial hard credit enhancement (CE) for the class A, B, C and D notes is 12.00%, 9.50%, 7.25% and 5.25%, respectively. CE levels for classes A, B and C are lower than for DEFT 2023-2 but similar to levels seen in the three prior transactions. All classes benefit from 2.58% per annum of excess spread. The structure can support the default of the top 10, eight, six and four non-IG obligors.

Operational and Servicing Risk ? Quality of Origination, Underwriting and Servicing: DFS has demonstrated adequate abilities as originator, underwriter and servicer, as evidenced by historical delinquency and loss performance of securitized trusts and the managed portfolio.

RATING SENSITIVITIES

Factors that Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Negative Rating Action/Downgrade

Unanticipated increases in the frequency of defaults could produce CNL levels higher than the base case and would likely result in declines of CE and remaining net loss coverage levels available to the notes. Additionally, unanticipated declines in recoveries could also result in a decline in net loss coverage. Decreased net loss coverage may make certain note ratings susceptible to potential negative rating actions, depending on the extent of the decline in coverage.

Fitch conducts a sensitivity of the obligor concentration coverage approach in which the ratings of the top 20 obligors were assumed to have been downgraded by a single rating category. For example, an obligor currently rated 'BBB' would be downgraded to 'BB'. No rating migration applies to unrated entities, as they were already categorized as non-IG in Fitch's primary analysis. The results of this analysis showed that all of the classes would experience a multi-notch downgrade. The severity of these downgrades is driven by the 'BBB' range obligors being downgraded to non-IG.

The top 20 obligors downgraded to non-IG increases to nine from one. This results in higher loss hurdles when compared with the primary scenario and the ratings to the DEFT 2023-3 notes would be downgraded. Fitch considers this analysis conservative, as it does not take into consideration the build in enhancement as the transaction de-levers. In reality, downgrades of entities occur over a longer period, which would give the transaction time to de-lever as the collateral pool amortizes. Furthermore, Fitch considers the likelihood of a simultaneous downgrade of these entities unlikely and, therefore, views this scenario as remote.

Fitch conducts sensitivity analyses by stressing both a transaction's initial base case CNL and recovery rate assumptions and examining the rating implications on all classes of issued notes. The CNL sensitivity stresses the CNL proxy to the level necessary to reduce each rating by one full category, to non-IG (BBsf) and to 'CCCsf' based on the break-even loss coverage provided by the CE structure. Additionally, Fitch applies 1.5x and 2.0x increases to the CNL proxy, which represent moderate and severe stresses, respectively.

Fitch also evaluates the impact of stressed recovery rates on an equipment ABS structure and rating impact with a 50% haircut. However, Fitch's rating analysis for DEFT 2023-3 only assumes a 3.50% recovery credit. Given the low recovery assumption, Fitch did not conduct a recovery rate sensitivity for this rating analysis.

Factors that Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Positive Rating Action/Upgrade

Stable to improved asset performance driven by stable delinquencies and defaults would lead to increasing CE levels and consideration for potential upgrades.

Fitch conducted a sensitivity of the aforementioned obligor concentration coverage approach in which the ratings of the top 20 obligors were assumed to have been upgraded by a single rating category. For example, an obligor currently rated 'BBB-' was assumed to have been upgraded to 'A-' at close. No rating migration applies to unrated entities, as they were already categorized as non-IG in Fitch's primary analysis. This results in lower loss hurdles when compared to the primary scenario and the commensurate ratings would remain unchanged.

CRITERIA VARIATION

Model Implied Rating: The 2023-3 analysis incorporates criteria variations to Fitch's "U.S. Equipment Lease and Loan ABS Rating Criteria." Under Fitch's criteria, the committee's rating determination may deviate from the model-implied-rating (MIR) by up to one full rating category (three rating notches) due to qualitative considerations such as asset performance or the transaction's structure.

The variation relates to the 2023-3 class C notes having a MIR of 'AAAsf', which is two categories above the assigned rating of 'Asf'. Fitch believes that this criteria variation is warranted due to high obligor concentration risk, class C's significant reliance upon the excess spread and its sensitivity to the downgrade of top obligors.

USE OF THIRD PARTY DUE DILIGENCE PURSUANT TO SEC RULE 17G -10

Fitch was provided with Form ABS Due Diligence-15E (Form 15E) as prepared by PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP. The third-party due diligence described in Form 15E focused on the comparison and recomputation of certain information with respect to 175 contracts from the preliminary collateral pool of assets in connection with DEFT 2023-3. Fitch considered this information in its analysis and it did not have an effect on Fitch's analysis or conclusions.

Fitch Expects to Rate Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2023-3; Issues Presale
3040 words
4 October 2023
Fitch Rating / Non Rating Action Commentary
FITRA
English
Copyright 2023 by Fitch Ratings Inc., Fitch Ratings Ltd. and its subsidiaries.

Related Content:

Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2023-3 (US ABS): https://app.fitchconnect.com/search/research/article/RPT_10248234 [https://app.fitchconnect.com/search/research/article/RPT_10248234]

Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2023-3 - Appendix: https://app.fitchconnect.com/search/research/article/RPT_10248414 [https://app.fitchconnect.com/search/research/article/RPT_10248414]

Fitch Ratings-New York-04 October 2023: Fitch Ratings expects to assign ratings and Rating Outlooks to the notes issued by Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2023-3 (DEFT 2023-3). The transaction is a securitization of equipment receivables originated by Dell Financial Services L.L.C. (DFS) or its affiliates.

Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2023-3

----A1 ; Short Term Rating; Expected Rating; F1+(EXP)sf

----A2 ; Long Term Rating; Expected Rating; AAA(EXP)sf; Rating Outlook Stable

----A3 ; Long Term Rating; Expected Rating; AAA(EXP)sf; Rating Outlook Stable

----B ; Long Term Rating; Expected Rating; AA(EXP)sf; Rating Outlook Stable

----C ; Long Term Rating; Expected Rating; A(EXP)sf; Rating Outlook Stable

----D ; Long Term Rating; Expected Rating; BBB(EXP)sf; Rating Outlook Stable

KEY RATING DRIVERS

Collateral/Obligor Performance ? Strong Credit Quality: Consistent with prior DEFT transactions, DEFT 2023-3 has a high concentration of investment-grade (IG) obligors. The weighted-average (WA) rating of the top 10 rated obligors is about 'A-'/'BBB+', stronger than the two recent transactions in 2023. Although the amount of non-IG obligors in DEFT 2023-3 is lower than in recent transactions, there remains a sizable portion, but these obligors have historically demonstrated low default and loss experience.

Concentration Risk ? Obligor Concentration: The largest obligor, the top-10 obligors and the top 20 obligors represent 4.69%, 28.69% and 39.93% of DEFT 2023-3, respectively. These levels are lower than DEFT 2023-2 and 2023-1 transactions. While there is high concentration within the top 10 obligors, concentration declines significantly after that and is more consistent with traditional small-ticket equipment ABS transactions. Furthermore, the top 10 obligors are mostly IG entities.

Given the unique collateral characteristics of DEFT transactions, a modified obligor concentration approach is the primary rating driver as opposed to the stressed loss approach.

Forward-Looking Approach to Derive Base-Case Loss Proxy ? Strong but Normalizing Asset Performance: Loss performance in the small and medium business (SMB) segment remains strong, at or below the portfolio's historical average, improving from the weakness in the late 2020 and early 2021. The public and large institutions (PLI) segment has seen low default rates due to the sturdy credit profiles of these obligors. All DFS-sponsored securitizations showed low cumulative net losses (CNLs), but performance of recent DEFT transactions has shown a normalizing trend compared with the strength shown through the pandemic.

The base case CNL proxy for DEFT 2023-3 is 1.20%, but the ratings are determined based on a modified obligor coverage approach given the transaction's high concentration of IG obligors among the top 20 obligors and shorter contract terms than those of other equipment ABS.

Structural Analysis ? Sufficient Credit Enhancement: All classes benefit from a cash reserve account and overcollateralization (OC). Total initial hard credit enhancement (CE) for the class A, B, C and D notes is 12.00%, 9.50%, 7.25% and 5.25%, respectively. CE levels for classes A, B and C are lower than for DEFT 2023-2 but similar to levels seen in prior three transactions. All classes benefit from 2.18% per annum of excess spread. The structure can support the default of the top 10, eight, six and four non-IG obligors.

Operational and Servicing Risk ? Quality of Origination, Underwriting and Servicing: DFS has demonstrated adequate abilities as originator, underwriter and servicer, as evidenced by historical delinquency and loss performance of securitized trusts and the managed portfolio.

RATING SENSITIVITIES

Factors that Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Negative Rating Action/Downgrade

Unanticipated increases in the frequency of defaults could produce CNL levels higher than the base case and would likely result in declines of CE and remaining net loss coverage levels available to the notes. Additionally, unanticipated declines in recoveries could also result in a decline in net loss coverage. Decreased net loss coverage may make certain note ratings susceptible to potential negative rating actions, depending on the extent of the decline in coverage.

Fitch conducts a sensitivity of the obligor concentration coverage approach in which the ratings of the top 20 obligors were assumed to have been downgraded by a single rating category. For example, an obligor currently rated 'BBB' would be downgraded to 'BB'. No rating migration applies to unrated entities, as they were already categorized as non-IG in Fitch's primary analysis. The results of this analysis showed that all of the classes would experience a multi-notch downgrade. The severity of these downgrades is driven by the 'BBB' range obligors being downgraded to non-IG.

The top 20 obligors downgraded to non-IG increases to nine from one. This results in higher loss hurdles when compared with the primary scenario and the ratings to the DEFT 2023-3 notes would be downgraded. Fitch considers this analysis conservative, as it does not take into consideration the build in enhancement as the transaction de-levers. In reality, downgrades of entities occur over a longer period, which would give the transaction time to de-lever as the collateral pool amortizes. Furthermore, Fitch considers the likelihood of a simultaneous downgrade of these entities unlikely and, therefore, views this scenario as remote.

Fitch conducts sensitivity analyses by stressing both a transaction's initial base case CNL and recovery rate assumptions and examining the rating implications on all classes of issued notes. The CNL sensitivity stresses the CNL proxy to the level necessary to reduce each rating by one full category, to non-IG (BBsf) and to 'CCCsf' based on the break-even loss coverage provided by the CE structure. Additionally, Fitch applies 1.5x and 2.0x increases to the CNL proxy, which represent moderate and severe stresses, respectively.

Fitch also evaluates the impact of stressed recovery rates on an equipment ABS structure and rating impact with a 50% haircut. However, Fitch's rating analysis for DEFT 2023-3 only assumes a 3.50% recovery credit. Given the low recovery assumption, Fitch did not conduct a recovery rate sensitivity for this rating analysis.

Factors that Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Positive Rating Action/Upgrade

Stable to improved asset performance driven by stable delinquencies and defaults would lead to increasing CE levels and consideration for potential upgrades.

Fitch conducted a sensitivity of the aforementioned obligor concentration coverage approach in which the ratings of the top 20 obligors were assumed to have been upgraded by a single rating category. For example, an obligor currently rated 'BBB-' was assumed to have been upgraded to 'A-' at close. No rating migration applies to unrated entities, as they were already categorized as non-IG in Fitch's primary analysis. This results in lower loss hurdles when compared to the primary scenario and the commensurate ratings would remain unchanged.

The third-party due diligence described in Form 15E focused on the comparison and recomputation of certain information with respect to 175 contracts from the preliminary collateral pool of assets in connection with DEFT 2023-3. Fitch considered this information in its analysis and it did not have an effect on Fitch's analysis or conclusions.

Fitch Rates Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2023-2
3019 words
22 June 2023
Fitch Rating / Non Rating Action Commentary
FITRA
English
Copyright 2023 by Fitch Ratings Inc., Fitch Ratings Ltd. and its subsidiaries.

Fitch Ratings-New York-22 June 2023: Fitch Ratings has assigned ratings and Rating Outlooks to the notes issued by Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2023-2 (DEFT 2023-2). The transaction is a securitization of equipment receivables originated by Dell Financial Services L.L.C. (DFS) or its affiliates.

Dell Equipment Finance Trust 2023-2

----A-1 ; Short Term Rating; New Rating; F1+sf

----A-2 ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; AAAsf; Rating Outlook Stable

----A-3 ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; AAAsf; Rating Outlook Stable

----B ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; AAsf; Rating Outlook Stable

----C ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; Asf; Rating Outlook Stable

----D ; Long Term Rating; New Rating; BBBsf; Rating Outlook Stable

KEY RATING DRIVERS

Collateral/Obligor Performance ? Strong Credit Quality: Consistent with prior DEFT transactions, DEFT 2023-2 has a high concentration of investment-grade (IG) obligors. The weighted average (WA) rating of the top-10 rated obligors is about 'BBB+'/'BBB', consistent with DEFT 2023-1 and other recent DEFT transactions. There is a large portion of non-IG obligors, but these obligors have historically demonstrated low default and loss experience.

Concentration Risk ? Obligor Concentration: The largest obligor, the top-10 obligors and the top-20 obligors represent 4.71%, 30.51% and 44.90% of DEFT 2023-2, respectively. These levels are in line with DEFT 2023-1 and prior 2021 and 2020 DEFT transactions. While there is high concentration within the top-15 obligors, concentration declines significantly after that and is more consistent with traditional small-ticket equipment ABS transactions. The top-15 obligors are mostly IG entities.

Given the unique collateral characteristics of DEFT transactions, a modified obligor concentration approach is the primary rating driver as opposed to the stressed loss approach.

Forward-Looking Approach to Derive Base-Case Loss Proxy ? Strong but Normalizing Asset Performance: Loss performance in the small and medium business (SMB) segment remains strong, at or below the portfolio's historical average, improving from the weakness in late 2020 and early 2021. The public and large institutions (PLI) segment has seen low default rates due to the sturdy credit profiles of these obligors. All DFS-sponsored securitizations exhibited low cumulative net losses (CNLs), but performance of recent DEFT transactions has shown a normalizing trend compared with the strength exhibited through the COVID-19 pandemic.

The base case CNL proxy for DEFT 2023-2 is 1.20%, but the ratings are determined based on a modified obligor coverage approach given the transaction's high concentration of IG obligors among the top-20 obligors and shorter contract terms compared to those of other equipment ABS transactions.

Structural Analysis ? Sufficient Credit Enhancement: All classes benefit from a cash reserve account and overcollateralization (OC). Total initial hard credit enhancement (CE) for the class A, B, C and D notes is 13.65%, 12.60%, 10.35% and 6.90%, respectively. CE levels for classes A, B and C are higher than for DEFT 2023-1 and the 2022 transactions. All classes benefit from 2.69% per annum of excess spread. The structure can support the default of the top-10, eight, six and four non-IG obligors.

Operational and Servicing Risk ? Quality of Origination, Underwriting and Servicing: DFS has demonstrated adequate abilities as originator, underwriter and servicer, as evidenced by historical delinquency and loss performance of securitized trusts and the managed portfolio.

RATING SENSITIVITIES

Factors that Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Negative Rating Action/Downgrade

Unanticipated increases in the frequency of defaults could produce CNL levels higher than the base case and would likely result in declines of CE and remaining net loss coverage levels available to the notes. Additionally, unanticipated declines in recoveries could also result in a decline in net loss coverage. Decreased net loss coverage may make certain note ratings susceptible to potential negative rating actions, depending on the extent of the decline in coverage.

Fitch conducts a sensitivity of the obligor concentration coverage approach in which the ratings of the top 20 obligors were assumed to have been downgraded by a single rating category. For example, an obligor currently rated 'BBB' would be downgraded to 'BB'. No rating migration applies to unrated entities, as they were already categorized as non-IG in Fitch's primary analysis. The results of this analysis showed that all of the classes would experience a multi-notch downgrade. The severity of these downgrades is driven by the 'BBB' range obligors being downgraded to non-IG.

The top 20 obligors downgraded to non-IG increases to 13 from six. This results in higher loss hurdles when compared with the primary scenario and the ratings to the DEFT 2023-2 notes would be downgraded. Fitch considers this analysis conservative, as it does not take into consideration the build in enhancement as the transaction de-levers. In reality, downgrades of entities occur over a longer period, which would give the transaction time to de-lever as the collateral pool amortizes. Fitch considers the likelihood of a simultaneous downgrade of these entities unlikely and, therefore, views this scenario as remote.

Fitch conducts sensitivity analyses by stressing both a transaction's initial base case CNL and recovery rate assumptions and examining the rating implications on all classes of issued notes. The CNL sensitivity stresses the CNL proxy to the level necessary to reduce each rating by one full category, to non-IG (BBsf) and to 'CCCsf' based on the break-even loss coverage provided by the CE structure. Additionally, Fitch applies 1.5x and 2.0x increases to the CNL proxy, which represent moderate and severe stresses, respectively.

Fitch also evaluates the impact of stressed recovery rates on an equipment ABS structure and rating impact with a 50% haircut. However, Fitch's rating analysis for DEFT 2023-2 only assumes a 3.50% recovery credit. Given the low recovery assumption, Fitch did not conduct a recovery rate sensitivity for this rating analysis.

Factors that Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Positive Rating Action/Upgrade

Stable to improved asset performance driven by stable delinquencies and defaults would lead to increasing CE levels and consideration for potential upgrades.

Fitch conducted a sensitivity of the aforementioned obligor concentration coverage approach in which the ratings of the top 20 obligors were assumed to have been upgraded by a single rating category. For example, an obligor currently rated 'BBB-' was assumed to have been upgraded to 'A-' at close. No rating migration applies to unrated entities, as they were already categorized as non-IG in Fitch's primary analysis. This results in lower loss hurdles when compared to the primary scenario and the commensurate ratings would remain unchanged.

Best/Worst Case Rating Scenario

International scale credit ratings of Structured Finance transactions have a best-case rating upgrade scenario (defined as the 99th percentile of rating transitions, measured in a positive direction) of seven notches over a three-year rating horizon; and a worst-case rating downgrade scenario (defined as the 99th percentile of rating transitions, measured in a negative direction) of seven notches over three years. The complete span of best- and worst-case scenario credit ratings for all rating categories ranges from 'AAAsf' to 'Dsf'. Best- and worst-case scenario credit ratings are based on historical performance. For more information about the methodology used to determine sector-specific best- and worst-case scenario credit ratings, visit https://www.fitchratings.com/site/re/10111579 [https://www.fitchratings.com/site/re/10111579].

USE OF THIRD PARTY DUE DILIGENCE PURSUANT TO SEC RULE 17G -10

Fitch was provided with Form ABS Due Diligence-15E (Form 15E) as prepared by PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP. The third-party due diligence described in Form 15E focused on the comparison and recomputation of certain information with respect to 175 contracts from the preliminary collateral pool of assets in connection with DEFT 2023-2. Fitch considered this information in its analysis and it did not have an effect on Fitch's analysis or conclusions.

REFERENCES FOR SUBSTANTIALLY MATERIAL SOURCE CITED AS KEY DRIVER OF RATING

The principal sources of information used in the analysis are described in the Applicable Criteria.

REPRESENTATIONS, WARRANTIES AND ENFORCEMENT MECHANISMS

A description of the transaction's representations, warranties and enforcement mechanisms (RW&Es) that are disclosed in the offering document and which relate to the underlying asset pool is available by clicking the link to the Appendix. The appendix also contains a comparison of these RW&Es to those Fitch considers typical for the asset class as detailed in the Special Report titled 'Representations, Warranties and Enforcement Mechanisms in Global Structured Finance Transactions'.

ESG Considerations

Unless otherwise disclosed in this section, the highest level of ESG credit relevance is a score of '3'. This means ESG issues are credit-neutral or have only a minimal credit impact on the entity, either due to their nature or the way in which they are being managed by the entity. For more information on Fitch's ESG Relevance Scores, visit www.fitchratings.com/esg's[http://www.fitchratings.com/esg's] ESG Relevance Scores, visit

This results in higher loss hurdles when compared with the primary scenario and the ratings to the DEFT 2023-2 notes would be downgraded. Fitch considers this analysis conservative, as it does not take into consideration the build in enhancement as the transaction de-levers. In reality, downgrades of entities occur over a longer period, which would give the transaction time to de-lever as the collateral pool amortizes. Furthermore, Fitch considers the likelihood of a simultaneous downgrade of these entities unlikely and, therefore, views this scenario as remote.

Fitch conducts sensitivity analyses by stressing both a transaction's initial base case CNL and recovery rate assumptions and examining the rating implications on all classes of issued notes. The CNL sensitivity stresses the CNL proxy to the level necessary to reduce each rating by one full category, to non-IG (BBsf) and to 'CCCsf' based on the break-even loss coverage provided by the CE structure. Additionally, Fitch applies 1.5x and 2.0x increases to the CNL proxy, which represent moderate and severe stresses, respectively.

Fitch also evaluates the impact of stressed recovery rates on an equipment ABS structure and rating impact with a 50% haircut. However, Fitch's rating analysis for DEFT 2023-2 only assumes a 3.50% recovery credit. Given the low recovery assumption, Fitch did not conduct a recovery rate sensitivity for this rating analysis.

Factors that Could, Individually or Collectively, Lead to Positive Rating Action/Upgrade

Stable to improved asset performance driven by stable delinquencies and defaults would lead to increasing CE levels and consideration for potential upgrades.

Fitch conducted a sensitivity of the aforementioned obligor concentration coverage approach in which the ratings of the top 20 obligors were assumed to have been upgraded by a single rating category. For example, an obligor currently rated 'BBB-' was assumed to have been upgraded to 'A-' at close. No rating migration applies to unrated entities, as they were already categorized as non-IG in Fitch's primary analysis. This results in lower loss hurdles when compared to the primary scenario and the commensurate ratings would remain unchanged.

Best/Worst Case Rating Scenario

International scale credit ratings of Structured Finance transactions have a best-case rating upgrade scenario (defined as the 99th percentile of rating transitions, measured in a positive direction) of seven notches over a three-year rating horizon; and a worst-case rating downgrade scenario (defined as the 99th percentile of rating transitions, measured in a negative direction) of seven notches over three years. The complete span of best- and worst-case scenario credit ratings for all rating categories ranges from 'AAAsf' to 'Dsf'. Best- and worst-case scenario credit ratings are based on historical performance. For more information about the methodology used to determine sector-specific best- and worst-case scenario credit ratings, visit https://www.fitchratings.com/site/re/10111579 [https://www.fitchratings.com/site/re/10111579].

USE OF THIRD PARTY DUE DILIGENCE PURSUANT TO SEC RULE 17G -10

Fitch was provided with Form ABS Due Diligence-15E ("Form 15E") as prepared by PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP. The third-party due diligence described in Form 15E focused on the comparison and recomputation of certain information with respect to 175 contracts from the preliminary collateral pool of assets in connection with DEFT 2023-2. Fitch considered this information in its analysis and it did not have an effect on Fitch's analysis or conclusions.

Fitch Rates Senior Notes Issued by Dell International and EMC 'BBB'
2636 words
10 January 2023
Fitch Rating / Non Rating Action Commentary
FITRA
English
Copyright 2023 by Fitch Ratings Inc., Fitch Ratings Ltd. and its subsidiaries.

Fitch Ratings-Chicago-10 January 2023: Fitch Ratings has rated co-issuers, Dell International LLC's and EMC Corp.'s, senior notes 'BBB'. The senior notes will be pari passu with Dell's senior unsecured obligations. Fitch expects the transaction to be leverage neutral and the companies will use net proceeds to repay $1 billion of 5.45% senior notes due June 2023 and any remaining net proceeds for corporate purposes, including the repayment of other debt.

Key Rating Drivers

Strengthened Financial Profile: Dell's strengthened financial profile with solid adjusted FCF and low core leverage (core debt/core EBITDA) provides flexibility as the company faces nearer-term headwinds from weakening PC shipments and enterprise infrastructure spending amidst concerns over recession. Over the longer term, Fitch expects modest but consistent organic revenue growth and the company to sustain profit margins and cash flow metrics, which should enable the company to maintain target core credit metrics of 1.5x-2.0x.

PC Market Leader: Fitch expects Dell to continue outperforming the PC market through share consolidation on top of stronger and more resilient than previously expected market growth. Dell's computing solutions group (CSG) segment is poised for another year of double-digit growth from solid consumer PC demand and recovering commercial markets. Scale-driven market consolidation by the top three PC makers, including Dell, should continue to fuel growth for this business, despite long-held risks of PC market maturation.

Challenging Demand Environment: Fitch expects challenging infrastructure spending dynamics will constrain growth for Dell's infrastructure solutions group (ISG) segment. Fitch forecasts low-single-digit growth for ISG, but demand for infrastructure spending will remain volatile and constrained by customer hybrid infrastructure-optimization trends. Meanwhile, Fitch expects macroeconomic headwinds and digestion of robust demand for PCs during the COVID-19 pandemic will weigh on near-term revenue.

Standalone Profitability Profile: Fitch expects Dell's profit margins will moderate from peak levels in recent years over the near term, due to macroeconomic headwinds, including higher input prices. The resumption of ISG and commercial PC growth should drive modest profit margin expansion over the longer term, although Fitch forecasts core EBITDA margins will remain in the high-single digits, down from 10% in in recent years.

Derivation Summary

Dell's credit profile is in-line with the 'BBB' rating, with the company's strong financial structure and flexibility, diversification and scale-based competitive advantages offsetting mature growth dynamics and comparatively low profitability. Fitch believes Dell's business profile is well-positioned compared with IT hardware provider peers, including Hewlett Packard Enterprise Company (HPE; BBB+/Stable) and HP Inc. (BBB+/Stable), given the scale and diversification of its installed base.

Dell's financial structure is in line with that of HPE, with Dell's slightly stronger and more consistent cash flow profile offset by HPE's higher profit margins due to Dell's nearly two-thirds mix of PC and peripherals sales. Dell's operating profile is equally positioned to that of HP, which has a comparable PC business and faces secular challenges in its printing business. However, HP's financial profile is stronger, with higher FCF margins and a more conservative financial structure.

Dell's 'BBB' Long-Term IDR maps to either 'F2' or 'F3' short-term ratings under Fitch's Corporate Rating Criteria and Fitch believes Dell's financial flexibility factor is in-line with the minimum 'bbb+' that is required for the higher of the two short-term ratings. Fitch's criteria emphasizes the liquidity sub-factor, which has strengthened considerably now that core debt maturities should be easily manageable with core FCF through the forecast period. The 'F2' short-term rating also reflects Dell comfortably meeting the criteria's requirement of at least a 'bbb-' financial structure and 'a-' operating environment factor score.

Key Assumptions

--Dell's revenue declines by low- to mid-single digits in fiscal 2023 and 2024, reflecting weaker demand, particularly in PCs;

--Revenue grows by low single digits through the remainder of the forecast period from ongoing market-share gains;

--Profitability moderates in fiscal 2023 and remains challenged in fiscal 2024 before expanding with a sales mix shift to ISG;

--Dell uses cash flow for a combination of shareholder returns and debt reduction.

RATING SENSITIVITIES

Factors that could, individually or collectively, lead to positive rating action/upgrade:

--Expectations for core leverage at or below 2.0x and adjusted pre-dividend FCF to core debt sustained near 30%;

--Consistent organic revenue growth from profitable market-share gains in CSG and ISG segments.

Factors that could, individually or collectively, lead to negative rating action/downgrade:

--Expectations for core leverage sustained above 2.5x and adjusted pre-dividend FCF to core debt sustained near 20%;

--Decline in organic revenue from sustained market-share losses in CSG and ISG segments.

Best/Worst Case Rating Scenario

International scale credit ratings of Non-Financial Corporate issuers have a best-case rating upgrade scenario (defined as the 99th percentile of rating transitions, measured in a positive direction) of three notches over a three-year rating horizon; and a worst-case rating downgrade scenario (defined as the 99th percentile of rating transitions, measured in a negative direction) of four notches over three years. The complete span of best- and worst-case scenario credit ratings for all rating categories ranges from 'AAA' to 'D'. Best- and worst-case scenario credit ratings are based on historical performance. For more information about the methodology used to determine sector-specific best- and worst-case scenario credit ratings, visit https://www.fitchratings.com/site/re/10111579[https://www.fitchratings.com/site/re/10111579].

Liquidity and Debt Structure

Adequate Liquidity: Fitch believes Dell's liquidity should remain adequate and, as of Oct. 28, 2022, was supported by $4.9 billion of cash and cash equivalents and an undrawn $6 billion revolving credit facility expiring in 2027, which Fitch expects will back-stop Dell's CP program. Fitch's forecast for $3.5 billion to $4.5 billion of annual adjusted FCF also supports liquidity.

Issuer Profile

Dell is a leading global diversified technology infrastructure provider, with a comprehensive portfolio of IT hardware, software and service solutions spanning both traditional and emerging, multi-cloud technologies.

Summary of Financial Adjustments

Fitch calculates core metrics for Dell, which exclude the impact of the capital financing business, Dell Financial Services (DFS). Fitch applies a maximum allowable leverage ratio for DFS of 4:1 to financing receivables as part of its core debt estimation. Fitch also excludes changes in DFS financing receivables to arrive at adjust cash flow metrics.

ESG Considerations

Unless otherwise disclosed in this section, the highest level of ESG credit relevance is a score of '3'. This means ESG issues are credit-neutral or have only a minimal credit impact on the entity, either due to their nature or the way in which they are being managed by the entity. For more information on Fitch's ESG Relevance Scores, visit www.fitchratings.com/esg[http://www.fitchratings.com/esg]

Fitch Affirms Dell Technologies at 'BBB' and Assigns 'F2' Short-Term Ratings; Outlook Stable
2804 words
18 July 2022
Fitch Rating / Non Rating Action Commentary
FITRA
English
Copyright 2022 by Fitch Ratings Inc., Fitch Ratings Ltd. and its subsidiaries.

Fitch Ratings-Chicago-18 July 2022: Fitch Ratings has affirmed the 'BBB' long-term ratings for Dell Technologies, Inc. (Parent) and its subsidiaries, Dell International LLC and EMC Corp. (Co-borrowers), as well as the 'BBB' Long-Term Issuer Default Rating (IDR) and 'BBB-' senior unsecured ratings for Dell, Inc. (Legacy notes). Fitch has also assigned a 'F2' Short-Term IDR to the parent and the co-borrowers and 'F2' rating to the co-borrowers' CP program. The Rating Outlook is Stable.

The CP program authorizes up to $5 billion of borrowings by the co-borrowers and Fitch expects the company's $5 billion revolving credit facility due Nov. 1, 2026 will back-stop the program. The CP program is guaranteed by Dell Technologies, Inc., Denali Intermediate, Inc. and Dell, Inc.

Key Rating Drivers

Strengthened Financial Profile: Dell's strengthened financial profile with solid adjusted FCF and low core leverage (core debt/core EBITDA), provides flexibility as the company faces nearer-term headwinds from weakening PC shipments and enterprise infrastructure spending amidst concerns over recession. Over the longer term, Fitch expects modest but consistent organic revenue growth and the company to sustain profit margins and cash flow metrics, which should enable the company to maintain target core credit metrics of 1.5x-2.0x.

PC Market Leader: Fitch expects Dell to continue outperforming the PC market through share consolidation on top of stronger and more resilient than previously expected market growth. Dell's computing solutions group (CSG) segment is poised for another year of double-digit growth from solid consumer PC demand and recovering commercial markets. Scale-driven market consolidation by the top three PC makers, including Dell, should continue to fuel growth for this business, despite long-held risks of PC market maturation.

Challenging Infrastructure Spending Dynamics: Fitch expects challenging infrastructure spending dynamics will constrain growth for Dell's infrastructure solutions group (ISG) segment. Fitch forecasts low-single-digit growth for ISG but demand for infrastructure spending will remain volatile and constrained by customer hybrid infrastructure-optimization trends.

Standalone Profitability Profile: Fitch expects Dell's profit margins will moderate from peak levels in recent years over the near term, due to macroeconomic headwinds and normalization of operating expenses from actions taken during the pandemic. The resumption of ISG and commercial PC growth should drive modest profit margin expansion over the longer term, although Fitch forecasts core EBITDA margins will remain near 9%, down from 10% in in recent years.

Derivation Summary

Dell's credit profile is in-line with the 'BBB' rating, with the company's strong financial structure and flexibility, diversification and scale-based competitive advantages offsetting mature growth dynamics and comparatively low profitability. Fitch believes Dell's business profile is well-positioned compared with IT hardware provider peers, including Hewlett Packard Enterprise Company (HPE; BBB+/Stable) and HP Inc. (BBB+/Stable), given the scale and diversification of its installed base.

Dell's financial structure is in line with that of HPE, with Dell's slightly stronger and more consistent cash flow profile offset by HPE's higher profit margins due to Dell's nearly two-thirds mix of PC and peripherals sales. Dell's operating profile is equally positioned to that of HP, which has a comparable PC business and faces secular challenges in its printing business. However, HP's financial profile is stronger, with higher FCF margins and a more conservative financial structure.

Dell's 'BBB' Long-Term IDR maps to either 'F2' or 'F3' short-term ratings under Fitch's Corporate Rating Criteria and Fitch believes Dell's financial flexibility factor is in-line with the minimum 'bbb+' that is required for the higher of the two short-term ratings. Fitch's criteria emphasizes the liquidity sub-factor, which has strengthened considerably now that core debt maturities should be easily manageable with core FCF through the forecast period. The 'F2' short-term also reflects Dell comfortably meeting the criteria's requirement of at least a 'bbb-' financial structure and 'a-' operating environment factor score.

Key Assumptions

--Dell's revenue declines by low-single-digit decline in fiscal 2023, reflecting a weakening PC market.

--Revenue grows by low single digits through the remainder of the forecast period from ongoing market-share gains.

--Profitability moderates in fiscal 2023 and gradually expands with a shift in ISG mix.

--Dell cash flow for a combination of shareholder returns, including a potential and debt reduction.

RATING SENSITIVITIES

Factors that could, individually or collectively, lead to positive rating action/upgrade:

--Expectations for core leverage at or below 2.0x and adjusted pre-dividend FCF to core debt sustained near 30%.

--Consistent organic revenue growth from profitable market-share gains in CSG and ISG segments.

Factors that could, individually or collectively, lead to negative rating action/downgrade:

--Expectations for core leverage sustained above 2.5x and adjusted pre-dividend FCF to core debt sustained near 20%.

--Decline in organic revenue from sustained market-share losses in CSG and ISG segments.

Best/Worst Case Rating Scenario

International scale credit ratings of Non-Financial Corporate issuers have a best-case rating upgrade scenario (defined as the 99th percentile of rating transitions, measured in a positive direction) of three notches over a three-year rating horizon; and a worst-case rating downgrade scenario (defined as the 99th percentile of rating transitions, measured in a negative direction) of four notches over three years. The complete span of best- and worst-case scenario credit ratings for all rating categories ranges from 'AAA' to 'D'. Best- and worst-case scenario credit ratings are based on historical performance. For more information about the methodology used to determine sector-specific best- and worst-case scenario credit ratings, visit https://www.fitchratings.com/site/re/10111579[https://www.fitchratings.com/site/re/10111579].

Liquidity and Debt Structure

Adequate Liquidity: Fitch believes Dell's liquidity should remain adequate and, as of April 29, 2022, was supported by $6.7 billion of cash and cash equivalents and an undrawn $5 billion revolving credit facility expiring on Nov. 1, 2026, which Fitch expects will back-stop Dell's CP program. Fitch's forecast for $3.5 billion to $4.5 billion of adjusted FCF also supports liquidity.

Issuer Profile

Dell is a leading global diversified technology infrastructure provider, with a comprehensive portfolio of IT hardware, software and service solutions spanning both traditional and emerging, multi-cloud technologies.

Summary of Financial Adjustments

Aside from standard financial statement adjustments, Fitch calculates core metrics for Dell, which exclude the impact of the capital financing business, Dell Financial Services (DFS). Upon Fitch's upgrade of Dell to 'BBB' in connection with the company's separation from VMware and subsequent deleveraging, Fitch increased the maximum allowable leverage for DFS to 4:1 from 3:1. Fitch applies this multiple to financing receivables as part of its core debt estimation.

Fitch Assigns 'BBB' Rating to Dell International's and EMC's Senior Notes Offering
2743 words
6 December 2021
Fitch Rating / Non Rating Action Commentary
FITRA
English
Copyright 2021 by Fitch Ratings Inc., Fitch Ratings Ltd. and its subsidiaries.

Fitch Ratings-Chicago-06 December 2021: Fitch Ratings has assigned 'BBB' ratings to the senior unsecured notes offering of co-issuers, Dell International LLC and EMC Corp. The notes will be pari passu with the co-issuers' existing senior unsecured debt, other than EMC's legacy senior notes. Fitch expects Dell will use net proceeds to fund the tender, including premiums, primarily for senior notes due 2036 and 2046, a transaction announced in conjunction with the new senior notes offering.

The ratings reflect Dell's strengthened financial structure and flexibility from the company's use of cash flow and net proceeds from the tax-free spin-off of VMware, Inc. for debt reduction. This, in conjunction with a solid demand environment, results in Fitch-estimates core debt to core EBITDA (core leverage), which exclude the impact of Dell's captive financing unit, approaching 2.0x in the near term. In addition, Dell's FCF will be available for a mix of investments in growth and capital returns, even as it continues reducing debt to achieve its long-term core leverage target of 1.5x.

Key Rating Drivers

Strengthened Balance Sheet: Dell used its $9.3 billion-$9.7 billion pro rata share of VMware's $11.5 billion dividend paid in connection with the spin-off for debt reduction. As a result, pro forma credit metrics in-line with a strong 'BBB' rating with core debt to operating EBITDA below 2.5x and approaching 2.0x in fiscal 2023 and heading toward Dell's longer-term 1.5x core leverage target. With profitability more in-line with a strong 'BB' rating balanced against a financial profile more in-line with a weak 'A' rating, Fitch believes Dell's overall credit profile is consistent with a 'BBB' Long-Term Issuer Default Rating (IDR).

Solid PC Business Momentum: Fitch expects Dell to continue outperforming the PC market through share consolidation on top of stronger and more resilient than previously expected market growth. Dell's computing solutions group (CSG) segment is poised for another year of double-digit growth from solid consumer PC demand and recovering commercial markets. Scale-driven market consolidation by the top three PC makers, including Dell, should continue to fuel growth for this business, despite long-held risks of PC market maturation.

Challenging Infrastructure Spending Dynamics: Fitch expects challenging infrastructure spending dynamics will constrain growth for Dell's infrastructure solutions group (ISG) segment, although Fitch forecasts spending will recover in fiscal 2H22 after significant demand constraints in fiscal 2021 due to pandemic-driven lockdowns. While Fitch forecasts low-single-digit growth for ISG in fiscal 2022, demand for infrastructure spending will remain volatile and constrained to low-single-digit average growth by customer hybrid infrastructure-optimization trends.

Standalone Profitability Profile: Fitch expects Dell's post-spin-off profit margins will moderate in fiscal 2022 from peak levels in recent years, due in large part to normalization of cost actions during the pandemic and continued momentum in lower-margin consumer PCs. The resumption of ISG and commercial PC growth should drive modest profit margin expansion beginning in fiscal 2023, although Fitch forecasts core EBITDA margins will remain near 9%, versus nearly 10% in fiscal 2020-2021 and FCF margins adjusted for Dell Financial Services LLC receivables change in the low- to mid-single digits.

Derivation Summary

Dell's credit profile is in-line with the 'BBB' rating, with the company's strong financial structure and flexibility, diversification and scale-based competitive advantages offsetting mature growth dynamics and comparatively low profitability. Fitch believes Dell's business profile is well-positioned compared with IT hardware provider peers, including Hewlett Packard Enterprise Company (HPE; BBB+/Negative) and HP Inc. (BBB+/Stable), given the scale and diversification of its installed base.

Following the spin-off, Dell's financial structure is in line with that of HPE, with Dell's slightly stronger and more consistent cash flow profile offset by HPE's higher profit margins due to Dell's nearly two-thirds mix of PC and peripherals sales. Dell's operating profile is equally positioned to that of HP, which has a comparable PC business and faces secular challenges in its printing business. However, HP's financial profile is stronger, with higher FCF margins and a more conservative financial structure.

Key Assumptions

--Dell's revenue grows by nearly 10% in fiscal 2022, followed by a mid-single-digit decline in fiscal 2023, reflecting VMware's full-year separation;

--On a standalone basis, Dell's revenue grows by low single digits in fiscal 2021-2025, from ongoing market share gains in CSG and a gradually improving infrastructure-spending environment as PC demand moderates;

--Profitability moderates in fiscal 2022 and gradually expands with a shift in ISG mix and normalizing input costs;

--Dell uses 40%-60% of adjusted pre-dividend FCF for capital returns balanced against ongoing debt reduction to achieve target core leverage.

RATING SENSITIVITIES

Factors that could, individually or collectively, lead to positive rating action/upgrade:

--Expectations for core leverage at or below 2.0x and adjusted pre-dividend FCF to core debt sustained near 30%.

--Consistent organic revenue growth from profitable market-share gains in CSG and ISG segments.

Factors that could, individually or collectively, lead to negative rating action/downgrade:

--Expectations for core leverage sustained above 2.5x and adjusted pre-dividend FCF to core debt sustained near 20%.

--Decline in organic revenue from sustained market-share losses in CSG and ISG segments.

Best/Worst Case Rating Scenario

International scale credit ratings of Non-Financial Corporate issuers have a best-case rating upgrade scenario (defined as the 99th percentile of rating transitions, measured in a positive direction) of three notches over a three-year rating horizon; and a worst-case rating downgrade scenario (defined as the 99th percentile of rating transitions, measured in a negative direction) of four notches over three years. The complete span of best- and worst-case scenario credit ratings for all rating categories ranges from 'AAA' to 'D'. Best- and worst-case scenario credit ratings are based on historical performance. For more information about the methodology used to determine sector-specific best- and worst-case scenario credit ratings, visit https://www.fitchratings.com/site/re/10111579[https://www.fitchratings.com/site/re/10111579].

Liquidity and Debt Structure

Adequate Liquidity: Fitch believes Dell's liquidity should remain adequate. It was supported by $11.5 billion of cash and cash equivalents as of Oct. 29, 2021, along with an undrawn $3.0 billion senior unsecured revolving credit facility expiring in 2026. Fitch's forecast of $3.5 billion-$4.5 billion of adjusted FCF also supports liquidity.

ESG CONSIDERATIONS

Unless otherwise disclosed in this section, the highest level of ESG credit relevance is a score of '3'. This means ESG issues are credit-neutral or have only a minimal credit impact on the entity, either due to their nature or the way in which they are being managed by the entity. For more information on Fitch's ESG Relevance Scores, visit www.fitchratings.com/esg[http://www.fitchratings.com/esg].

Issuer Profile

Dell is a leading global diversified technology infrastructure provider, with a comprehensive portfolio of IT hardware, software and service solutions spanning both traditional and emerging, multi-cloud technologies.

Summary of Financial Adjustments

Fitch applies a maximum allowable debt-to-equity ratio of 4:1 to Dell's financing receivables to allocate a portion of total debt to DFS, which Fitch excludes from measuring core debt. Fitch similarly excludes DFS profitability from total EBITDA to calculate core EBITDA, as well as the change in financing receivables from FFO in calculating adjusted FCF.

Fitch Upgrades Dell to 'BBB'; Resolves Positive Watch
2900 words
1 November 2021
Fitch Rating / Non Rating Action Commentary
FITRA
English
Copyright 2021 by Fitch Ratings Inc., Fitch Ratings Ltd. and its subsidiaries.

Fitch Ratings-Chicago-01 November 2021: Fitch Ratings has resolved the Rating Watch Positive on the ratings for Dell Technologies, Inc. and its subsidiaries in connection with the company's completion of the VMware, Inc. spin-off and upgraded the Long-Term Issuer Default Ratings (IDR) to 'BBB' from 'BBB-'.

Fitch has affirmed the first-lien secured ratings at 'BBB' in anticipation of the collateral supporting the first-lien debt falling away and leaving it pari passu with Dell's non-legacy senior unsecured obligations, including Dell International LLC's senior unsecured notes, which Fitch has upgraded to 'BBB' from 'BBB-'. Finally, Fitch has upgraded the structurally subordinated legacy senior notes of Dell Inc. to 'BBB-' from 'BB+'. A Stable Rating Outlook has been assigned.

The ratings reflect Dell's meaningfully strengthened credit profile following the company's ongoing use of cash flow and net proceeds from the tax-free spin-off of VMware, Inc. for debt reduction. Dell has reduced debt by $6.5 billion fiscal year-to-date and, in conjunction with stronger than expected operating results, Fitch-estimates core debt to core EBITDA, which exclude the impact of Dell's captive financing unit, are below 2.5x following the spin-off and will approach 2.0x in the near term.

Key Rating Drivers

Significant Debt Reduction: Dell will use its approximately $9.3 billion-$9.7 billion pro rata share of VMware's $11.5 billion dividend paid in connection with the spin-off for debt reduction. As a result, pro forma credit metrics will be in-line with a strong 'BBB' rating with core debt to operating EBITDA below 2.5x and approaching 2.0x in fiscal 2023 and heading toward Dell's longer-term 1.5x core leverage target. With profitability more in-line with a strong 'BB' rating balanced against a financial profile more in-line with a weak 'A' rating, Fitch believes Dell's overall credit profile is consistent with a 'BBB' LT IDR.

The spin-off simplifies VMware's ownership structure and results in Dell shareholders' proforma ownership interest in VMware just under 30% and Michael Dell and Silver Lake Partners (SLP) just over 40% and 10%, respectively. Dell also announced that it has entered into a partnership with VMware aimed at joint collaboration and product development, leveraging Dell's go-to-market (GTM) scale, other cross-selling opportunities and Dell's captive financing business (DFS). The partnership is set to last five years from close with automatic one-year renewals thereafter and should remain additive to Dell's top line.

Solid PC Business Momentum: Fitch expects Dell to continue outperforming the PC market through share consolidation on top of stronger and more resilient than previously expected market growth. Dell's computing solutions group (CSG) segment is poised for another year of double-digit growth from solid consumer PC demand and recovering commercial markets. Scale-driven market consolidation by the top three PC makers, including Dell, should continue to fuel growth for this business, despite long-held risks of PC market maturation.

Challenging Infrastructure Spending Dynamics: Fitch expects challenging infrastructure spending dynamics will constrain growth for Dell's infrastructure solutions group (ISG) segment, although Fitch forecasts spending will recover in fiscal 2H22 after significant demand constraints in fiscal 2021 due to pandemic-driven lockdowns. While Fitch forecasts low-single-digit growth for ISG in fiscal 2022, demand for infrastructure spending will remain volatile and constrained to low-single-digit average growth by customer hybrid infrastructure-optimization trends.

Standalone Profitability Profile: Fitch expects Dell's post-spin-off profit margins will moderate in fiscal 2022 from peak levels in recent years, due in large part to normalization of cost actions during the pandemic and continued momentum in lower-margin consumer PCs. The resumption of ISG and commercial PC growth should drive modest profit margin expansion beginning in fiscal 2023, although Fitch forecasts core EBITDA margins will remain near 9%, versus nearly 10% in fiscal 2020-2021 and FCF margins adjusted for Dell Financial Services LLC receivables change in the low- to mid-single digits.

Derivation Summary

Dell's credit profile is in-line with the 'BBB' rating, with the company's strong financial structure and flexibility, diversification and scale-based competitive advantages offsetting mature growth dynamics and comparatively low profitability. Fitch believes Dell's business profile is well-positioned compared with IT hardware provider peers, including Hewlett Packard Enterprise Company (HPE; BBB+/Negative) and HP Inc. (BBB+/Stable), given the scale and diversification of its installed base.

Following the spin-off, Dell's financial structure is in line with that of HPE, with Dell's slightly stronger and more consistent cash flow profile offset by HPE's higher profit margins due to Dell's nearly two-thirds mix of PC and peripherals sales. Dell's operating profile is equally positioned to that of HP, which has a comparable PC business and faces secular challenges in its printing business. However, HP's financial profile is stronger, with higher FCF margins and a more conservative financial structure.

Key Assumptions

--Dell's revenue grows by nearly 10% in fiscal 2022, followed by a mid-single-digit decline in fiscal 2023, reflecting VMware's full-year separation;

--On a standalone basis, Dell's revenue grows by low single digits in fiscal 2021-2025, from ongoing market share gains in CSG and a gradually improving infrastructure-spending environment as PC demand moderates;

--Profitability moderates in fiscal 2022 and gradually expands with a shift in ISG mix and normalizing input costs;

--Dell uses cash flow for debt reduction to achieve target core leverage, with excess cash flow for stock buybacks and dividends rather than large-scale acquisitions thereafter.

RATING SENSITIVITIES

Factors that could, individually or collectively, lead to positive rating action/upgrade:

--Expectations for core leverage at or below 2.0x and adjusted pre-dividend FCF to core debt sustained near 30%.

--Consistent organic revenue growth from profitable market-share gains in CSG and ISG segments.

Factors that could, individually or collectively, lead to negative rating action/downgrade:

--Expectations for core leverage sustained above 2.5x and adjusted pre-dividend FCF to core debt sustained near 20%.

--Decline in organic revenue from sustained market-share losses in CSG and ISG segments.

Best/Worst Case Rating Scenario

International scale credit ratings of Non-Financial Corporate issuers have a best-case rating upgrade scenario (defined as the 99th percentile of rating transitions, measured in a positive direction) of three notches over a three-year rating horizon; and a worst-case rating downgrade scenario (defined as the 99th percentile of rating transitions, measured in a negative direction) of four notches over three years. The complete span of best- and worst-case scenario credit ratings for all rating categories ranges from 'AAA' to 'D'. Best- and worst-case scenario credit ratings are based on historical performance. For more information about the methodology used to determine sector-specific best- and worst-case scenario credit ratings, visit https://www.fitchratings.com/site/re/10111579[https://www.fitchratings.com/site/re/10111579].

Liquidity and Debt Structure

Adequate Liquidity: Fitch believes Dell's liquidity should remain adequate. It was supported by $5.8 billion of cash and cash equivalents as of July 30, 2021, along with an undrawn $4.5 billion of first lien senior secured revolving credit facility (RCF) expiring in September 2023. Fitch's forecast of $3.5 billion-$4.5 billion of adjusted FCF also supports liquidity.

Issuer Profile

Dell is a leading global diversified technology infrastructure provider, with a comprehensive portfolio of IT hardware, software and service solutions spanning both traditional and emerging, multi-cloud technologies.

REFERENCES FOR SUBSTANTIALLY MATERIAL SOURCE CITED AS KEY DRIVER OF RATING

The principal sources of information used in the analysis are described in the Applicable Criteria.

ESG Considerations

Unless otherwise disclosed in this section, the highest level of ESG credit relevance is a score of '3'. This means ESG issues are credit-neutral or have only a minimal credit impact on the entity, either due to their nature or the way in which they are being managed by the entity. For more information on Fitch's ESG Relevance Scores, visit www.fitchratings.com/esg[http://www.fitchratings.com/esg]
